‚ÄúIn the end, what was it you were doing, sire?‚Äù she asked.

‚ÄúOh, well... we were making exactly what you see here,‚Äù he said. There were three bowls sitting on the table Souma pointed to. ‚ÄúIn the world I come from, it‚Äôs called ramen.‚Äù

‚ÄúRamen... is it?‚Äù

As Souma had said, the three bowls were filled with ramen. What was more, it was the oily kind made with seafood and pork bones. Souma offhandedly thrust his chopsticks into a bowl and began slurping the noodles noisily.

‚ÄúYep... The soup is almost perfect. But since we‚Äôre using gelin udon, it‚Äôs a little bland.‚Äù

‚ÄúThere‚Äôs no helping that. Right now, wheat is precious, yes.‚Äù

‚ÄúAll the more reason to resolve the food crisis quickly...‚Äù

While watching Souma and Poncho talk, Serina tried her own ramen. Wrapping the noodles around her fork like pasta, she put them into her mouth.

When she did, the rich, savory flavor of the seafood and pork bone broth surged forward. It was thick, rich, and it had punch, yet the taste of the vegetables had melted into the broth, keeping it from being too rich. What a complex flavor this was. It was greasy, yet her instincts demanded another mouthful.

Souma and Poncho watched Serina, smiling.

‚ÄúI was wondering if we might be able to use the bones and vegetable scraps we would otherwise throw away to make a soup, you see,‚Äù Souma said. ‚ÄúI had Poncho studying it. He did it late at night like this, so we wouldn‚Äôt disturb the cooks.‚Äù

‚ÄúOh, it was a lot of hard work, yes,‚Äù Poncho said. ‚ÄúIt was a dish I had never eaten for myself, after all.‚Äù

‚ÄúI see... so this was the truth behind the necromancer, then,‚Äù Serina said, wiping her mouth with a napkin. ‚ÄúStill, this is delicious. ...Sir Poncho?‚Äù

‚ÄúY-Yes. What is it?‚Äù

‚ÄúCould I trouble you to teach me how to make this soup?‚Äù

‚ÄúOf course you can, yes.‚Äù

It seemed that Serina, too, had been charmed by the magic of this oily soup.

After that, a ghost story spread saying that there were two necromancers.

At almost the same time, Serina, whose skin had become oddly smooth (an effect of the collagen?) said, ‚ÄúSir Poncho, about the bones you use in that soup, why not burn and crush them to powder before putting them in?‚Äù

‚ÄúTh-That makes sense! I‚Äôm impressed, Serina! You look at things differently, yes!‚Äù

‚ÄúTonight... If you have the chance to try it, let me taste some.‚Äù

‚ÄúOf course I will, yes.‚Äù

When the maids saw the two of them speaking intimately like this, their imaginations ran wild, but that is a story for another time.

Chapter 4: A Day Off in Parnam

It was a few weeks after the first episode of The King‚Äôs Brillunch had been broadcast.

That day, a petition was delivered to Prime Minister Hakuya Kwonmin.

The personnel department had been the ones to organize it, but it included names from the royal guard, the maid force, and every other group within the palace. Marx, who was now the chamberlain, and Ludwin, the head of the royal guard, had put their names on it, as well.

Wondering what it could be, Hakuya quickly perused the contents to find...

‚Äú...Ah, I see.‚Äù

Hakuya agreed with the petition despite himself.

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

‚ÄúSo, there you have it. I will be insisting you take time off, sire,‚Äù Hakuya said.

‚ÄúThere I have what, exactly?‚Äù I asked. ‚ÄúI still can‚Äôt make heads or tails of what‚Äôs going on.‚Äù

While I had been working in the governmental affairs office, Hakuya had suddenly come in and said, ‚ÄúTake time off.‚Äù Then he‚Äôd casually dropped the bundle of papers he was holding onto the desk I‚Äôd been working at.

‚ÄúThis is a petition I received from the personnel department,‚Äù he informed me. ‚ÄúAccording to it, ‚ÄòWhen those at the top do not rest, those below them find it difficult to take time off.‚Äô You will find Sir Marx and Ludwin‚Äôs names on here, and I, your humble servant, have added my own name, as well.‚Äù

Ah... Now that he mentions it, I haven‚Äôt taken time off since being summoned here, have I? I thought.

It wasn‚Äôt that I wasn‚Äôt resting at all. Recently, now that I had gotten used to using Living Poltergeists, I‚Äôd sometimes left the paperwork to my ability and gone to do things like make dolls in Liscia‚Äôs room. If I let part of my mind work while part of it rested, I could work 24/7 without feeling the slightest bit exhausted. However, according to Hakuya, it seemed that wasn‚Äôt the issue here.

‚ÄúEven if you are resting, you are always in the palace, correct?‚Äù he asked me.

‚ÄúYeah, just in case anything happens.‚Äù

‚ÄúI am telling you that it does not look like you are resting when you do that. And, because it does not look like you are resting, everyone else finds it difficult to rest themselves. Please, understand that.‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs easy for you to say...‚Äù I said.

‚ÄúNormally, I would want you to take a large block of days off to rest,‚Äù he said, ‚Äúbut...‚Äù

‚ÄúDo we have that kind of time?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúWe do not.‚Äù

‚ÄúI figured...‚Äù

As a matter of fact, there was a mountain of things that needed doing. Expanding and strengthening the military, meeting with VIPs, creating documents for external use, pushing forward all sorts of reforms... the list could go on forever. Even Aisha‚Äôs request that I go to the God-Protected Forest as soon as possible was on hold at this point. Though I had at least told them how periodic thinning worked. A large park in the center of the royal capital, Parnam.

First, water from the river that ran near Parnam had been drawn into the first layer, which served as an underground aqueduct. That water was now being used in wells and public bath houses that once relied on underground water. The third layer was used as a sewer, ultimately emptying out into sedimentation ponds outside the capital where the sewage would be filtered before being returned to the river once more. ‚ÄúW-We‚Äôre childhood friends.‚Äù

‚ÄúChildhood friends... I see.‚Äù

From the way they‚Äôd been talking and acting, I had seen signs of their affection for each other, but... Well, there was no reason to point it out here.

‚ÄúIf you‚Äôre childhood friends, you must care more for one another than you would just any other person,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúAnd? If you join the Three Dukedoms, what do you plan to do about her?‚Äù

‚ÄúWhat do you mean, what will I do...? About what?‚Äù

‚ÄúWe‚Äôre imagining that the Three Dukedoms win. In that case, I may have been struck down, and you may even have been the one to take my severed head.‚Äù

‚ÄúHah! I‚Äôd be guaranteed a promotion, then!‚Äù

‚Äú...I suppose you would,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúSo, what of Kaede? A cute girl like her, in the losing army. When they find out, what will the soldiers of the winning side do...? As a soldier yourself, I think you can imagine, can‚Äôt you?‚Äù

When I pointed that out, Halbert visibly turned pale. Most likely, he was imagining ‚Äúthat sort‚Äù of scene. After the conclusion of a war, it wasn‚Äôt uncommon to see the defeated ravaged by the victors. Looting, arson, rape, slaughter... The madness of war was in that it allowed these acts of barbarity to happen.

Even so, Halbert raised his voice, as if trying to shake off his doubts. ‚ÄúDuke Carmine‚Äôs forces are well-organized! They would never do something so indecent!‚Äù

‚ÄúI don‚Äôt know what the situation is within the army, but Duke Carmine has more than just the regular forces in his duchy,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúThere are also those I stripped of their rights or investigated for corruption. Those nobles who‚Äôve raised the flag of rebellion against me. They have nothing to lose. If they lose, death for both them and their family line awaits. So they‚Äôll throw away their personal assets, hiring a large number of Zemish mercenaries.‚Äù

The mercenary state, Zem.

West of Amidonia and north of Turgis, it was a medium-sized country, founded by the mercenary commander Zem, who had used his wits to destroy the country which had hired him and then build his own nation of mercenaries in its place. They had declared themselves to be ‚Äúeternally neutral,‚Äù but their primary industry was dispatching mercenaries to other countries, so what that really meant was, ‚ÄúIf requested, we will dispatch mercenaries to any country.‚Äù Their mercenaries were ridiculously strong, so most countries recognized that it was better to have them as an ally than an enemy, and so they had formed mercenary contracts with them.

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs absurd! There are Zemish mercenaries under contract with the Forbidden Army, too! If they send mercenaries to the Three Dukedoms, as well, they‚Äôll be fighting against their own!‚Äù

‚ÄúOh, that won‚Äôt happen,‚Äù I assured him. ‚ÄúI terminated their employment contract with the Forbidden Army a while ago.‚Äù

Now seems like a good time, so let me talk about the military system of this country.

This kingdom had a total manpower of around 100,000 troops. They were divided like so:

40,000 in the army, led by Duke Georg Carmine.

10,000 in the navy, led by Duchess Excel Walter.

1,000 in the air force, led by Duke Castor Vargas.

(However, one wyvern knight was said to be equivalent to 100 soldiers from the army.)

Of these, only the air force had a knightly title bestowed on every one of its members (it was composed entirely of units of wyvern knights, i.e. ‚Äú1 wyvern + 1 or 2 knights,‚Äù so that was obvious), but more than half of the army and navy were made up of career soldiers. They trained day and night in the three duchies, and they received a salary from the three duchies.

You could say that the right to self-rule and the tax exemption on the profits from their lands, along with the many other special rights given to the three duchies, were there to support these troops.

Now, the remaining troops, numbering a little over 40,000, belonged to the Forbidden Army, but they were further divided beyond that.

There were the Royal Guard, who reported directly to the king, and the career soldiers who were attached to the Forbidden Army. Then there were the noble estates (which had less rights than the three duchies) and their personal forces on top of that. Also, due to our contract with the mercenary state, Zem, there had been a unit of mercenaries under the command of the Forbidden Army, as well, but I had already terminated their employment.

The reason that the Forbidden Army was smaller than the forces of the three duchies had to do with the concept behind this country.

This country had originally been born through many races working together. As a result, a member of the race with the largest population, a human, became the king, but in order to protect the rights of the other races, the commanders of the army, navy, and air forces would be chosen from the other races.

So, if a tyrant took the throne and began oppressing the other races, the system had been set up so that the armies of the Three Dukedoms, being larger than the Forbidden Army, could remove him. Turning that around, if one of the Three Dukedoms was plotting to usurp the throne, the system was set up in a way that if even one of the armies were to side with the king, the rebellion could be put down.

In a peaceful era, this might have been a good setup. However, now the Demon Lord‚Äôs Domain had appeared, and these were troubled times with every country looking for openings to take advantage of. With this sort of divided command structure, it was possible that we might not be able to respond quickly enough to a sudden crisis. As a matter of fact, I was trying to move forward with reforms, but the Three Dukedoms were giving me the silent treatment.

Now, let‚Äôs get back to how I released the mercenaries from their employment contracts.

‚ÄúHold on, what do you mean you released the Zemish mercenaries from their contracts?!‚Äù Liscia shouted.

‚ÄúOh, yeah, I hadn‚Äôt told you about that yet, had I?‚Äù I smiled wryly at the fact that, rather than Halbert, it was Liscia who voiced her surprise this time. ‚ÄúIt means exactly what it sounds like. Mercenaries are useless and just eat up money, you know.‚Äù

Machiavelli had said, ‚ÄúMercenaries and mixed armies are not to be trusted.‚Äù According to him, ‚ÄúMercenaries are tied to you only by their own profit; if presented with greater profit, they will easily betray you. Yet even when they fight, they protect their employer only for their own benefit, and so their loyalty is not to be expected. There is no reason to hire incapable mercenaries, and yet capable ones will always use their wits to seize their employer‚Äôs position.‚Äù

In fantasy novels and RPGs, protagonists with the mercenary job often appear, but the way the mercenary business actually worked was wildly different from the image you‚Äôll have seen there.

Basically, they were people who made their money on the battlefield. They held no loyalty to country or prince, quickly changing sides when the balance of benefits shifted.

In a losing battle, they fled immediately. Even when victorious, they would run wild. Compared to standing armies of the same size, their upkeep might cost less, but they were a negative in the long term.

‚ÄúWe don‚Äôt have the money to pay useless people like that,‚Äù I explained.

‚ÄúEven so, the mercenary contract was also proof of our friendly relations with Zem, you realize?!‚Äù Liscia shouted.

‚ÄúTrue, things have become tense with them since then, but you yourself said, ‚ÄòSpend always on defense, never on tribute,‚Äô didn‚Äôt you, Liscia? Unlike the empire, they can‚Äôt afford to invade us themselves. Paying them tribute to bide our time is pointless with them.‚Äù

The country was getting back at me by dispatching mercenaries to the Three Dukedoms, though.

I looked straight at Halbert. ‚ÄúThose blood-thirsty mercenaries are on the side of the Three Dukedoms. Do you think they‚Äôll leave a girl in the defeated army like Kaede alone? While Kaede is being tormented by the mercenaries, and they‚Äôre about to kill her because they‚Äôre done with her, where will you be, and what will you be doing?‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs...‚Äù Halbert hesitated.

That indecisive attitude of his got me steaming mad. ‚ÄúWill you be lifting my head aloft in joy?! Singing songs to celebrate your victory?! Meanwhile, your childhood friend may have been made their plaything, then left dead at the side of the road!‚Äù

‚ÄúUrkh...‚Äù

When I shouted at him, Halbert‚Äôs legs seemed to give out and he had to put his hands on the table for support. He had no comeback to that, and his mouth was closed tightly. Kaede watched him worriedly.

When I saw them like that... I calmed down a little. ‚ÄúHalbert Magna. The path you were about to choose is a dead end. If I win, you will be executed. If the Three Dukedoms win, Kaede will... Well, she may not come out of it all right. If you‚Äôre going to make the gamble of a lifetime, at least make sure the future you want is on the betting table.‚Äù

He said nothing.

‚ÄúBefore you do anything rash, always think back,‚Äù I told him. ‚ÄúThink about what is it that you wanted, what for, and for whom? Look around you, and think about it.‚Äù

‚ÄúWhat for... And for whom...‚Äù Halbert looked around.

His eyes met with Kaede‚Äôs, who was looking at him with concern. There were no words between them, but Halbert looked like a man released from whatever had been possessing him.

...What happens from here on is for them to decide, I thought.

‚ÄúSorry, Juna. We were getting in the way of your business, weren‚Äôt we?‚Äù I asked. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôll be leaving now.‚Äù

Just before we left, I went to apologize for making a scene, but Juna shook her head. ‚ÄúNo... Sire, your words carved themselves into my heart.‚Äù

After saying that, Juna seemed to hesitate for a moment. She clearly had something to say, but was unsure whether it was okay to say it.

I waited a little while, and finally Juna looked up, her face resolute. ‚ÄúSire... I have something to talk to you about.‚Äù

‚ÄúHey, Souma, there was something I wanted to ask,‚Äù Liscia said.

‚ÄúHm?‚Äù

We were inside the carriage we had called to take us back to the castle when Liscia, who was sitting beside me, asked a question.

Aisha was acting as the driver, so we were alone together in the carriage.

‚ÄúAbout what happened earlier,‚Äù she said. ‚ÄúYou were trying to persuade Halbert, right? When you said traitors would be judged by the law, you seemed kind of serious.‚Äù

‚Äú...Because he still hadn‚Äôt acted against me, yet. If he still does after this, I‚Äôm not going to show any mercy.‚Äù

‚ÄúIn the end, you‚Äôre still a nice guy, huh?‚Äù she said.

‚ÄúBe kind to your allies, severe with your enemies,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúThat‚Äôs the kind of king people want to support. It‚Äôs not like I‚Äôm being severe because I enjoy it. The fewer enemies we have, the better.‚Äù

‚ÄúJust like I thought... You‚Äôre a nice guy.‚Äù Liscia rested her head on my shoulder.

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

‚ÄîThe next day.

When I was in the governmental affairs office getting some paperwork done, Hakuya came in. Then, ‚ÄúThe head of the House of Magna, Sir Glaive Magna, has brought his son, Sir Halbert Magna, and Forbidden Army Mage Kaede Foxia, and is requesting an audience with you,‚Äù he reported to me.

...Sounds like there‚Äôs still another dispute to solve, I thought.

When I arrived in the audience chamber accompanied by Liscia and my bodyguard Aisha, there were already three people there kneeling. In front of the other two with his head lowered was a middle-aged man with salt and pepper hair. In his armor, he truly looked like a warrior who had seen many battles. Behind him were Kaede Foxia and Halbert Magna, who I had met the day before. That being the case, I deduced that this man in front of them with his head lowered must be Halbert‚Äôs father, Glaive.

‚ÄúRaise your heads, all three of you,‚Äù I said.

‚Äú‚ÄúYes, sir.‚Äù‚Äù

When Halbert and Kaede raised their heads, I found myself transfixed by the sight of Halbert‚Äôs face. I mean, he had the marks to show he‚Äôd been punched several times. His cheeks were swollen, and he had two black eyes. Those hadn‚Äôt been there when I‚Äôd seen him yesterday, so it must have happened after we‚Äôd parted.

‚ÄúHalbert... You‚Äôre looking even more handsome than last time I saw you,‚Äù I commented.

‚ÄúUrgh... Yes, sir!‚Äù A look of frustration crossed his face for a moment, but he didn‚Äôt fight back the way he had yesterday.

I wonder what happened to him after we parted yesterday.

I spoke to Glaive, whose head was still bowed. ‚ÄúGlaive Magna, raise your head.‚Äù

‚ÄúI humbly, humbly, beg you, show mercy for my son‚Äôs recent misconduct!‚Äù That was the lamentful response that came back. He was pressing his forehead against the floor. It was hard to tell since he had one knee up, but he was doing what we‚Äôd probably call a dogeza in Japan.

‚ÄúBy misconduct, do you mean what happened yesterday?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúYes, sir! I heard the details from Madam Kaede. While he may have been off-duty, he insulted you, sire, and what‚Äôs more, boasted that he would join the rebellious Three Dukedoms, which is utterly outrageous! ...However, my son is yet immature. He said those things because of his underdeveloped brain. Your anger is entirely justified, sire, but, please, let the blame fall on me for failing to educate him properly!‚Äù

Um... That was a little long winded, but what he‚Äôs saying is ‚ÄúI‚Äôll take the punishment, so please spare my son‚Äôs life,‚Äù I guess? I‚Äôm not even angry, though.

‚ÄúYesterday‚Äôs events happened when I was there in secret,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúI don‚Äôt intend to make a big deal out of it. From what I see here, he‚Äôs already been punished appropriately.‚Äù

‚ÄúSire, you are too kind.‚Äù Glaive apologized profusely, prostrating himself before me.

Halbert and Kaede hurriedly bowed their heads once more.

Finally, Glaive lifted his face. ‚ÄúNow then, sire. I realize this is incredibly rude, but I have come to tell you something.‚Äù

‚ÄúWhat?‚Äù

‚ÄúWell... It is something best not heard by many people...‚Äù

A secret, huh? I had Liscia, Aisha, Hakuya, Glaive, Halbert, and Kaede remain, then dismissed everyone else, including the guards. Aisha seemed out of place, but so long as she was here, if it turned out he was using the promise of secret information as a guise to assassinate me, I had someone to deal with that.

‚ÄúI‚Äôve cleared the room,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúSo, what is it you needed to tell me?‚Äù

‚ÄúYes, about that...‚Äù Glaive began to talk at a relaxed pace.

When we heard what it was he had to say, Halbert‚Äôs eyes went wide, Kaede looked down, gripping her fists tightly, Hakuya closed his eyes in silence, while Aisha looked around bewildered by everyone else‚Äôs reactions...

Liscia, meanwhile, had gone stiff and expressionless, not saying a word. There were tears streaming down her face.

As for me, it was a complicated feeling. Anger, exasperation, resignation, sadness... All those feelings got jumbled together in my chest, and I worked my hardest to keep them there.

I spoke in as calm and even a voice as I could manage, so as not to betray my feelings. ‚ÄúNow that you‚Äôve told me that... what do you want me to do about it?‚Äù

‚ÄúNothing. I just wanted you to be aware, sire.‚Äù

‚Äú...It‚Äôs heavy.‚Äù I stood up, giving orders to Kaede and Halbert. ‚ÄúForbidden Army Mage Kaede Foxia. This insight is too valuable, and dangerous, for me to leave you as a mere mage. I order you to serve under Ludwin of the Royal Guard as a staff officer.

‚ÄúHuh? Y-Yes, sir!‚Äù she exclaimed.

‚ÄúArmy Officer Halbert Magna. I order you to transfer to the Forbidden Army.‚Äù

‚ÄúHuh?! Me, join the Forbidden Army?!‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs right. You will be Kaede‚Äôs second-in-command and report to her. Her rank effectively makes her Number 2 in the Forbidden Army. Because she is still a young woman, there is the risk that her subordinates won‚Äôt take her seriously. In the event that that happens, you are to make sure they do as she says. Understood?‚Äù

‚Äú...Yes, sir!‚Äù

Thus, a new, young officer joined the Forbidden Army.

However, I wasn‚Äôt feeling emotionally at ease enough to be happy a new ally had joined us. As I forced down my violent emotions, my true feeling seep out through my gritted teeth just once.

‚ÄúHonestly, these people...‚Äù

Intermission 2: The Sighs of Duchess Excel Walter

Let‚Äôs talk about the system of nobility in this country.

Once you set aside royalty and the three dukes, the people can be divided into three groups: the nobles and knights, the commoners, and the slaves. (Refugees, as they are not citizens, do not fall into any of these groups.)

We will go into the institution of slavery on another occasion, but what divides the nobles and knights from the commoners is whether or not they hold land.

Because of that, the class of nobles and knights may also be referred to as lords, and the commoners who live on their lands may be referred to as their subjects. (Slaves are considered to be chattel, and thus are not included in this group.) Lords have a number of rights within their lands, and at the same time, they have military and other responsibilities to the country.

The titles and lands of the nobility and knighthood are generally hereditary, but commoners who distinguish themselves may be bestowed title and land by the country, raising them to knighthood (for those whose accomplishments are military) or nobility (for those whose accomplishments are in administration).

Furthermore, marrying into a noble or knightly family (in which case, the person provides their own land) is also possible. These people are referred to as new nobles or new knights.

This isn‚Äôt a distinction that formally exists, but certain hard-headed people who think of them as ‚Äúupstarts who were not born to be nobles or knights‚Äù refer to them this way. New nobles and new knights may pass their titles hereditarily. (Generally, a house becomes accepted after around three generations.)

Conversely, even nobles and knights can, if their crimes are great enough, be dropped to the rank of commoner or slave. In these cases, their lands and title are seized by the country and, in the worst cases, the entire house may lose their status. This is known as ‚Äúdestruction.‚Äù

The reason that, as noted earlier, nobles and knights distinguish themselves from new nobles and new knights is that they take pride in having maintained the status of their house and having avoided this ‚Äúdestruction‚Äù for three generations.

There is no need for the nobility and knighthood to manage their lands personally. Particularly with knights, who must spend most of the year serving in the military, management of their lands is left to the members of their household. Royal Guard Captain Ludwin Arcs was one example.

Furthermore, among the nobility, there are those who leave management of their lands to the members of their house, residing in Parnam where they serve in important posts such as top positions in the bureaucracy or as speaker in the Congress of the People. These people are called capital nobles, with the former prime minister (and current chamberlain) Marx being one example.

However, at present, the number of capital nobles had fallen to nearly half of what it had been the year before. The ones who had gone missing were those whose wrongdoing had been uncovered in Souma‚Äôs government spending audit. Those under investigation had been dismissed from their posts in the capital, and were under house arrest in their own lands.

For those whose crimes were minor, if they repaid the money they embezzled, and relinquished the family headship to another member of the family, their house would be allowed to continue, but for those whose crimes were great, all of their assets were seized and their house would be destroyed.

Of course, the sort of people who would engage in such corruption could not be expected to quietly acquiesce to the destruction of their houses. They took their personal forces and assets and attempted to flee.

However, because Souma and Hakuya could easily see their intentions, the borders were sealed, and they could not carry their assets out into other countries.

Unable to remain in their lands or flee to another country, ultimately, they headed for the duchy of Duke Carmine. They went to Georg Carmine, who was hostile to the king, and waited for an opportunity to rebel.

The central city of that Carmine Duchy was Randel.

While not as great in scale as the royal capital Parnam, it was still large compared to other cities, with a large enough population to become a city-state on its own.

General of the Army Georg Carmine‚Äôs castle was here, and a castle town had grown up around it. However, past generals had been indifferent to the city‚Äôs management and so, unlike Parnam which could change greatly with the direction the king chose to take it, the town had a nostalgic feel to it, probably the same now as it had been 100 years ago.

On a street corner in that city of Randel, a single carriage was parked. Inside the carriage was a beauty in her mid-twenties. Any man who saw her would, almost certainly, have let out a sigh of admiration.

Even wrapped as it was in a kimono that was similar in style to the ones worn in Japan, her voluptuous figure was still apparent. However, the reptilian tail which stuck out from the buttocks of her kimono and the tiny antlers that sprouted out from beneath her blue hair made it clear that she wasn‚Äôt just an ordinary human.

From inside her carriage she was listening to the hustle and bustle of the town around her. There must have been a tavern nearby, because she could hear a group of drunkards grumbling quite clearly.

‚ÄúSeriously, that new king... Just who does he think we are...? Hic!‚Äù

‚ÄúIndeed. It is we who have supported this kingdom for so many long years.‚Äù

‚ÄúBut the king goes and ignores us, pushing forward policies on his own!‚Äù

‚ÄúWhy did King Albert leave the country to that whelp...?‚Äù

‚ÄúHis retainers are no better! They‚Äôre a bunch of inexperienced novices, too! What‚Äôs with that gloomy black-robed jerk?! What‚Äôs with that human pig?!‚Äù

‚ÄúHeh heh heh, I‚Äôm sure he only values those‚Äôre good at flattering him.‚Äù

‚ÄúThe young are prone to such things! He throws out experienced people like us, only listening to people who‚Äôll flatter him. A king like that won‚Äôt last long.‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs right! Let‚Äôs take this country back with our own hands!‚Äù

‚ÄúYeah! For the kingdom we love!‚Äù

‚Äú‚Äú‚ÄúFor the kingdom we love!‚Äù‚Äù‚Äù

For the kingdom, is it...? My, how they do like to run their mouths. The woman in the carriage sighed. Even that sigh was alluring.

You people are the ones who betrayed the country with your illegal acts. When it came time for you to face the law, you fled, so it certainly takes some gall for you to say the king threw you out. And the king only values those who flatter him? Were you not watching when he gathered personnel? That king would use even those who were dissatisfied with him so long as they were worth it. He uses Sir Hakuya and Sir Poncho because they are capable. The reason he doesn‚Äôt use you is because you are not.

Since they didn‚Äôt even understand that much, she couldn‚Äôt bring herself to even bother ridiculing them.

It‚Äôs been a few months since the crown was transferred to His Majesty, Souma, yet he hasn‚Äôt made any major policy blunders or lost the support of the people. To the contrary, he‚Äôs shown extraordinary ability in the way he‚Äôs steadily resolving the food crisis we feared. No matter how much they respected King Albert for his sagacity, it‚Äôs nonsense to ask, ‚ÄúWhy did he choose that whelp?‚Äù

The woman rested her elbows on the windowsill, her chin in her hands.

To think the nobility has fallen so far from the proud and high-minded people who founded the country... Their ancestors must be turning in their graves.

Though she appeared to be in her mid-twenties, this woman recalled the dawning age of this kingdom more than 500 years ago. She thought back to her comrades, smiling sadly.

As a descendent of sea serpents, it would be more than another 500 years before she would be taken to their side.

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs times like this when belonging to a long-lived race is the hardest. I‚Äôve gotten used to bidding farewell to the short-lived, but then I‚Äôm forced to see unpleasant things like this. I envy you people who have been able to die without a care for what would come after.‚Äù

With those words, Navy Admiral Excel Walter, one of the three dukes, gave a self-deprecating laugh.

‚ÄúSea Princess!‚Äù

When a voice addressed her from outside the carriage, Excel sat up straight. ‚Äú...Yes?‚Äù

‚ÄúMa‚Äôam, a report has arrived from Canaria,‚Äù the voice said.

‚ÄúShow it to me,‚Äù she commanded.

‚ÄúYes, ma‚Äôam. It is here.‚Äù The speaker pushed the documents through a gap in the carriage door.

Excel took the documents, opening them and perusing their contents. As she was reading through them, finally her face broke into a smile.

I see... So that‚Äôs how you‚Äôve judged him. Yet still, you wish to be at his side, you say. Hmm... That‚Äôs all well and good, but I do think the loving praise dripping from your writing is going to give me heartburn. Really, now... I have to envy your youth.

Excel froze the documents with a sigh, then let them go. The documents fell, shattering into pieces when they struck the carriage floor.

Allow me to correct myself. When you live so long, there are times when you‚Äôll find new light in the most unexpected of ways. This feeling is something you people who have died can never taste, isn‚Äôt it?

Serves you right.

Excel wore the smile of a young girl, not showing so much as a hint of her true age.

Chapter 5: The Legendary Old Man

In the audience chamber of Parnam Castle...

A large number of people were lined up in this place where the hero summoning and talent award ceremony had been held. These were the bureaucrats of the finance ministry.

Each wore an exhausted expression on his face.

Their cheeks were sunken, they had bags under their eyes, some wore dry smiles, while others looked to be on the verge of collapsing. Despite that, each and every one of them had a twinkle in his eye.

Theirs were the eyes of warriors who had survived a bloody battle.

Since I had become king and launched my reforms to save an economy that was on the brink of collapse, they had served as my hands and feet, working hard, like horses drawing a carriage. Anyone who had been working to enrich themselves had been dismissed, leaving only the serious ones behind. These were people who worked hard, reluctant to take time off even to sleep.

One of them might spend an entire day comparing the numbers between sets of documents, while another might spend most of the day on horseback, going around to ensure funds were being used correctly. They had been spending their days returning home only to sleep. No... many of them didn‚Äôt even return home, they just slept in the castle‚Äôs nap room, returning to work as soon as they woke.

Some had families.

Some had children.

Some were recently married.

However, the time they would have spent with their families... they cast aside, continuing to work.

The face of a wife dissatisfied that her husband put work before her, the face of a child lonely because his father wouldn‚Äôt play with him, the face of a newlywed wife sincerely concerned for her husband... They averted their eyes from these faces, telling themselves it was just for now, and worked diligently.

Earnestly trying to save this country from collapse.

Earnestly trying to protect those in this country whom they loved.

I looked down at them while sitting on the throne. I probably didn‚Äôt look much better than they did at this point. While I could rest unused parts of my consciousness in shifts, I was handling five times my regular workload and working round-the-clock. While my body might have been fine, I could feel my spirit being ground down.

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs a fine look you‚Äôve all got on your faces, now.‚Äù I rose, speaking to them in a quiet voice. Then I went down to them, placing my hand on one thin man‚Äôs shoulder. ‚ÄúYour eyes are hollow and lifeless. You‚Äôve got the face of a ghoul.‚Äù

They all said nothing.

‚ÄúI know how it‚Äôs been,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúThese days of forgoing sleep, fighting with the numbers day in and day out, ignoring the pleas of your families that you stop coming to the castle. Do you remember how before, when I talked about how the technology of this country was all messed up, I mentioned that there were steel battleships, only they were drawn by massive sea dragons? Bearing the name of the former king, it was the sole battleship in the possession of the Forbidden Army, and the flagship of the Royal Navy.

Its shape was similar to the Mikasa, which was the flagship of the Combined Fleet at the time of the Battle of Tsushima. Now seems like a good time, so let me explain about some of the imbalances in this country‚Äôs technology.

You might find it strange that a country which hadn‚Äôt even reached the industrial revolution had these sorts of near-modern warships. However, thanks to this world‚Äôs magic and mysterious creatures, they were able to do things they otherwise couldn‚Äôt.

Even if something is made of iron, if it‚Äôs been built with the proper calculations for buoyancy, it can be made to float. In other words, the outer frame of a battleship can be built even with Middle Ages technology. The reason they hadn‚Äôt been built until after the industrial revolution was because the engines that would be needed to move them didn‚Äôt exist. In an era where your only means of propelling a boat are catching the wind with sails or rowing with oars, an iron ship wouldn‚Äôt be able to do anything but float there.

However, in this world, there were powerful sea dragons that were strong enough to tow an iron ship. By training them to pull the ships, ocean navigation became possible. That was why iron ships were built.

It was the same for the large cannons aboard the battleship.

This world already had gunpowder. Now, that in and of itself wasn‚Äôt strange. Even on Earth, there are traces of gunpowder having been used that predate the appearance of black powder, which was one of China‚Äôs three great inventions. In the second century, during the time of Romance of the Three Kingdoms, the general defending Chencang used an explosive weapon (something like a firecracker) to pulverize the invading army led by Zhuge Liang‚Äôs weapons.

However, in this world, there were no arquebuses.

Because they had magic for their long-range attacks, they had never developed firearms. Furthermore, there were what were called ‚Äúattachable spells.‚Äù By attaching spells with various effects to an object, it could be made stronger or able to cut better. Because of these, weapons with higher mass, which could have more spells embedded in them, tended to be more powerful.

Thus, an arrow was stronger than a bullet, a spear stronger than an arrow. To explain further, with a bullet‚Äôs small mass, even if you embedded an attack spell in it, it couldn‚Äôt pierce a suit of plated armor with a defensive spell embedded in it. This world‚Äôs magic was said to come from mixing special waves emitted by people with a substance called magicium in the atmosphere to produce a variety of phenomena. Magicium had an elemental alignment (with the exception of darkness), and the composition of the magicium in the atmosphere was greatly influenced by the terrain. Over the water there was mostly water magicium, meaning magic from the other elements was weakened there... and so on for other areas.

Because of this, if they were to use magic in naval battles, all elements but water would be weakened, and they would end up in a situation where water elemental magic didn‚Äôt have a long enough range. ‚ÄúHave earth mages in the Forbidden Army prioritize working on it. It will have an impact on the building time, but there‚Äôs no other choice.‚Äù

‚ÄúUnderstood.‚Äù He nodded. ‚ÄúNow that I think of it, I‚Äôve heard that Duchess Walter‚Äôs coastal city has these things called seawalls. Should we make those here as well?‚Äù

‚ÄúSeawalls, huh... It‚Äôll hurt the view...‚Äù I gave that some consideration. ‚ÄúIf possible, I want this trade port to be usable as a tourist destination, as well. Besides, they wouldn‚Äôt be able to stand up to an unprecedentedly large tsunami, anyway.‚Äù

‚ÄúWe shouldn‚Äôt build them, then?‚Äù he asked.

‚Äú...Let‚Äôs see. Actually, I‚Äôd rather build a city that doesn‚Äôt rely on seawalls. It seems like the civil engineering and construction guild has an expert on flood control, so let‚Äôs summon him and get his opinion.‚Äù

‚ÄúUnderstood,‚Äù he said. ‚ÄúNow, as to the specifics of the city plan...‚Äù

‚ÄúThanks to old man Urup, we know roughly the area that the tsunami can reach,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôll avoid it when we place the residential, commercial, and industrial districts. Of course, that goes for important facilities like consulates, as well.‚Äù

‚ÄúYou‚Äôre not going to develop the area that the tsunami reaches?‚Äù he asked.

‚ÄúThe fishing harbor and wharf can‚Äôt go anywhere else. As for the rest, we‚Äôll develop it as a seaside park.‚Äù

‚ÄúI see. You‚Äôll develop on the assumption that it‚Äôs going to get washed away.‚Äù

‚ÄúYeah,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúOh, one other thing, old man Urup.‚Äù

‚ÄúHm? What is it?‚Äù

‚ÄúI‚Äôm going to make you a state-registered storyteller, so see to it that the Legend of the Sea God gets handed down, please. I‚Äôm going to make it a public service job that requires a certification, so work hard to train the next generation to tell the story before you die.‚Äù

‚ÄúM-Me, a public servant?!‚Äù he exclaimed.

‚ÄúYeah. In addition to the ‚ÄòDon‚Äôt build houses where the tsunami can reach‚Äô lesson from earlier, work in ‚ÄòIf you feel an earthquake, assume there will be a tsunami,‚Äô and ‚ÄòBecause a tsunami is coming, evacuate to high-ground,‚Äô as well. ‚Äú...Understood! I shall spend the rest of my life on it!‚Äù he cried.

‚ÄúGood. By the way, about the castle wall that will surround the city...‚Äù

Three men talked enthusiastically about the plan for the city. Liscia and Aisha watched them with wry smiles.

‚ÄúHis Majesty... looks like he‚Äôs enjoying himself,‚Äù Aisha commented.

‚ÄúHe is enjoying himself,‚Äù Liscia nodded. ‚ÄúCompared to hunting for funds, at least.‚Äù

‚ÄúHm? What is it, Princess?‚Äù Aisha asked.

‚ÄúNo. It‚Äôs nothing. ...Hey, Aisha.‚Äù

‚Äú...I see. Well, then. Let‚Äôs work to support Souma so he can keep smiling.‚Äù

At the time, I didn‚Äôt realize at all that a conversation like this had taken place.

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

Thirty years later, an earthquake and unprecedentedly large tsunami struck this area.

The land was inundated by turbid waters and many boats were washed out to sea, but surprisingly few lives were lost. Because everyone in the area had grown up hearing the Legend of the Sea God from the storytellers, they were able to begin evacuating as soon as they felt the earthquake.

After the disaster, a statue titled ‚ÄúThe King and the Old Man‚Äù was built in the seaside park.

It was a statue to commemorate the old man who, at the time of the new city‚Äôs construction, had risked his life to make a direct appeal to the king and tell him how to prepare for the tsunami, and the wise king who had listened to his plans. If the two of them could have heard, they‚Äôd have laughed wryly, saying, ‚ÄúThat‚Äôs over-embellishing it.‚Äù

Particularly for old man Urup, who had once been the storyteller, but now appeared in stories of his descendants as the Legendary Old Man, what sort of expression did he have on his face while he watched over them from the next world?

Chapter 6: Relief

I‚Äôm Halbert Magna, age 19.

I‚Äôm the eldest son of the Magna family, well known within the Elfrieden Kingdom land forces. I myself used to belong to them, but after some stuff happened, I was forced to transfer to the Forbidden Army.

To add insult to injury, my commanding officer was my childhood friend, the earth mage Kaede Foxia, who liked to end her sentences with ‚Äúyou know.‚Äù To think, now I had to take orders from her... I wished it was all just a joke.

On top of that, what was I doing now? Right now, rather than a sword, I was swinging an entrenching tool (a round-edged shovel which can also be used in close quarters combat) instead.

Marching orders had come for the Forbidden Army, and when I arrived on the site, I was tasked with piling up dirt, hollowing out the middle, pouring in a gooey liquid (?), reinforcing the sides with gravel, then planting saplings on either side. After that, I would set up the street lamps filled with the lightmoss that are common in the capital, the kind which absorb light during the day and are phosphorescent at night, repeating these same tasks over and over.

To sum it up simply, I was doing roadwork.

Summer had ended, but the sun was still hot, and I was digging up dirt and making piles with it over and over.

‚ÄúWhy... does the Forbidden Army... have to do... roadwork?‚Äù

‚ÄúYou there. Stop prattling and get to work, on the double.‚Äù

Wiping the sweat from my brow, I looked over to see Kaede standing on top of a simple scaffold, smacking the railing with her megaphone as she gave orders. She must have been feeling the heat pretty badly herself. Her trademark perky fox ears had drooped down like dog ears.

‚ÄúHey, Kaede, is this really...?‚Äù I began.

‚ÄúYou can‚Äôt do that!‚Äù she protested. ‚ÄúHal, you‚Äôre my subordinate, you know. You must address me properly as the site foreman.‚Äù

‚Äú...Foreman, is this really a job for the Forbidden Army?‚Äù

‚ÄúThis is the sort of work that the Forbidden Army does now, you know,‚Äù she answered.

‚ÄúSurely we could leave this stuff to construction workers.‚Äù

‚ÄúThere just aren‚Äôt enough of them, you know. This is part of a plan for a kingdom-wide road network, you know. We‚Äôve hired unemployed people from the capital as well, I hear, but we‚Äôre still so short of hands, I‚Äôd even ask a warcat to help.‚Äù

Even so, would you normally have the military do this sort of work? I thought.

‚ÄúBesides, we can‚Äôt have just construction workers come here alone, you know,‚Äù she said. ‚ÄúThe further you go from a settlement, the more powerful the wild creatures get, after all. And if we hired adventurers to protect them, it would cost a fortune.‚Äù

‚ÄúSo, in the end, we‚Äôre just cheap labor, is that it...?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúIf you understand that, then get to work, on the double,‚Äù she said.

‚ÄúYou‚Äôre an earth mage. Can‚Äôt you do this faster with magic?‚Äù

‚ÄúI can‚Äôt afford to expend my magic here, you know,‚Äù she said. ‚ÄúHal, are you going to dig tunnels through the mountains in my place?‚Äù

I said nothing.

I went back to my work of digging up dirt and piling it up.

It‚Äôs better than being forced to dig a tunnel without magic, at least, I thought. What kind of old-fashioned hard labor sentence is this...?

Noon came. We went back to the camp and were given a two-hour break.

Inside the tent we ate, chatted, or used the simple beds (they were no more than stretchers that had grown a little fur) to take an afternoon nap. Apparently that king strongly encouraged naps after eating. It was something about how it improved work efficiency.

So work in the Forbidden Army literally came with ‚Äúthree meals and a nap,‚Äù but... once people found out what kind of work was involved, there was no way they would be jealous of us.

Anyway, I wasn‚Äôt going to make it through the afternoon if I didn‚Äôt eat, so I wolfed down the lunchbox I had been supplied.

Today‚Äôs lunchbox was meat and vegetables between bread. Delicious.

The meat was lightly spiced, which felt like it helped relieve my exhaustion. It was apparently a dish called shogayaki which that king had come up with. It was a menu he was experimenting with now that the production of the seasonings the king was having the mystic wolves make for him ‚Äî ‚Äúmiso,‚Äù ‚Äúsoy sauce,‚Äù and ‚Äúmirin‚Äù ‚Äî had gotten on track.

In the Forbidden Army, we were often served the king‚Äôs experimental menus like this. The meals were one of the few things that made me happy that I had been forced to transfer to the Forbidden Army. The meals we‚Äôd gotten in the land forces had prioritized quantity over quality. The kind of thing you‚Äôd picture from the words ‚ÄúA Man‚Äôs Meal.‚Äù Honestly, eating here even once had been enough to convince me I didn‚Äôt want to go back.

‚ÄúThat king... If nothing else, I‚Äôve got to recognize his gift for cooking,‚Äù I admitted.

‚ÄúThey really are delicious, you know,‚Äù Kaede agreed. ‚ÄúThe dishes our king comes up with.‚Äù

At some point, Kaede had sat down next to me, and she was eating the same menu.

‚ÄúAlso, it‚Äôs incredible that we can eat fresh veggies every day, you know,‚Äù she continued. ‚ÄúThey come in from the closest village to here that‚Äôs hooked up to the castle by road. The reason roads are great is that they make it easy to maintain supply lines, you know.‚Äù

‚ÄúThe roads we‚Äôre building are being useful right away, huh?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúWith this transportation capacity, you can almost call the food crisis solved already, you know. We can bring food from the areas with a surplus to the areas where there are shortages. We‚Äôll be able to transport foods that we couldn‚Äôt before because they didn‚Äôt keep long enough.‚Äù

‚Äú...Is he doing this because he knows all that stuff?‚Äù I asked. ‚ÄúThat king, I mean.‚Äù

‚ÄúHe‚Äôs an incredible man, you know. His foresight is almost frightening.‚Äù

Well, I thought Kaede was pretty amazing for being able to understand all of that, too. She could be a bit silly in some ways, but Kaede had some pretty high base specs. She could use magic, and she was sharp, too. That was probably why she had been chosen by the king himself.

...As her childhood friend, it did frustrate me a little, though.

...I need to do my best, too.

‚ÄúWell, now that you‚Äôve eaten, will you be taking a nap, Hal?‚Äù she asked me.

‚ÄúWell... I am tired. Guess I will.‚Äù

‚ÄúIn that case, you can rest your head in my lap, you know,‚Äù she said.

‚ÄúBwuh!‚Äù I spewed my tea.

Everyone was suddenly looking our way. More than half of those glances were from men who clearly wanted to kill me.

Now, even though I‚Äôm biased as her childhood friend, Kaede is cute. It‚Äôs nothing to write home about, but her figure‚Äôs not bad, and those fox ears and tail really work in her favor. It wasn‚Äôt surprising that she was treated like an idol in the Forbidden Army.

The king had told me to serve under her so that the men wouldn‚Äôt look down on Kaede, but, honestly, I think that with one request from Kaede, these guys would gladly have gone to their deaths. That was why their murderous rage was directed at me, for being so close to her.

I coughed desperately. ‚ÄúWhat are you saying?!‚Äù

‚ÄúPeople were talking about how the princess did it for the king in the park in the capital a little while back, you know,‚Äù she said.

‚ÄúI‚Äôm amazed they could do that in a place where so many people could see...‚Äù

‚ÄúPeople are saying we‚Äôll have a royal heir by next year. Though, partly because the king is from another world, the betting pools for the heir‚Äôs name haven‚Äôt been able to narrow down a list of candidates.‚Äù

‚Äú...You‚Äôre talking an awful lot about something that‚Äôs none of your business,‚Äù a voice said.

‚ÄúYou‚Äôre right. It makes me wish you‚Äôd show a little more awareness of your position as king.‚Äù

‚ÄúKing‚Äôs orders: Don‚Äôt be so uptight and formal. Also, no more of that ‚ÄòYour Majesty‚Äô stuff. Souma‚Äôs fine.‚Äù

‚ÄúNo, but...‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs good. I was just thinking I‚Äôd like a guy my age who I can chat casually with,‚Äù King Souma... Souma... said, seeming satisfied.

‚ÄúRight this way, sire. I‚Äôll show you around.‚Äù I rose to my feet and saluted Souma.

Instant gelin udon. Now we were talking. I wasn‚Äôt going to let this chance to add some variety to our already-limited selection of field rations slip away.

The princess and Kaede seemed amused by my sudden change in attitude, but I didn‚Äôt let that bother me. Food was my number one priority, after all.

The five of us ‚Äî me, Kaede, Souma, the princess, and the dark elf guard ‚Äî arrived at a section of road that was currently being paved. There, Souma asked me to demonstrate the work procedures for everyone.

‚ÄúOnce he‚Äôs piled up the dirt on both sides, we pour that gooey stuff over there in the middle,‚Äù Souma said, explaining road construction to the princess.

‚ÄúRoman concrete... It‚Äôs a mixture of volcanic ash and lime. It will harden as time passes. It also has a unique viscosity, so it doesn‚Äôt crack easily. If you want to see how tough it is... Well, if you look at that over there, I think you‚Äôll understand.‚Äù

After saying that, Souma pointed to a giant lizard that was larger than many buildings. The giant lizard was towing a number of wheeled container cars behind it. The container cars were packed full of construction materials and provisions for the soldiers.

The giant lizard, rhinosaurus.

Also known as the great horned lizard, this super-sized lizard was distinctive for the two great tusks which grew from atop its nose. (If Souma had been describing it, he might have described it as, ‚ÄúTake a rhino, add a Komodo dragon, divide by two, then multiply the size by ten.‚Äù) They were omnivorous and gentle, easily becoming attached to people, so they were used in big cities to haul large volumes of cargo like this. ‚ÄúIt‚Äôs so tough that even if that rhinosaurus rammed it at full speed, it won‚Äôt crack,‚Äù Souma explained.

‚ÄúThat is incredible,‚Äù the princess said. ‚ÄúIt‚Äôs that hard?‚Äù

‚ÄúNo, actually, it‚Äôs flexible where it needs to be, so it distributes the force that‚Äôs put into it. In the world I came from, there were buildings made with this concrete over 2,000 years ago that were still standing.‚Äù

2,000 years? Four times longer than this country‚Äôs existed? I thought. Wow, that‚Äôs amazing.

‚ÄúMoving on, the street lamps he‚Äôs setting up on either side of the road are the same as the ones in the capital. ‚ÄúYes, sir! These warding trees constantly emit waves that monsters and wild animals dislike. They probably do it to keep giant boars from eating them. In the God-Protected Forest, we plant these warding trees densely around our villages in order to prevent incursions by monsters and animals.‚Äù

‚ÄúI see,‚Äù the princess mused. ‚ÄúThey‚Äôre like a simple barrier, huh.‚Äù

‚ÄúWhy? Wouldn‚Äôt it be better to stop them entirely?‚Äù the princess asked.

‚ÄúOkay then, Liscia. ‚ÄúI get that we absolutely shouldn‚Äôt do it, but why are your examples so specific?!‚Äù she asked.

What‚Äôs a ‚Äúlocal self-governing body‚Äù? I wondered.

Unlike me, Kaede seemed to understand, and she was thoroughly impressed.

‚ÄúWowwie... You‚Äôve thought it through that far. I should have expected no less from our king, you know,‚Äù she said.

‚ÄúHmm. Well, all I did was bring along a bunch of knowledge from the world I was in before,‚Äù Souma said.

Kaede‚Äôs eyes sparkled, and Souma blushed a little as she stared at him.

As she watched those two, the princess seemed a little miffed.

‚ÄúUm, Princess?‚Äù the dark elf asked.

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs one scary look you‚Äôve got on your face.‚Äù

‚ÄúI-Is it? ...Well, you‚Äôre not one to talk, are you?‚Äù

‚ÄúHuh?‚Äù

Then, at that moment...

‚ÄúNo!‚Äù

...there was a sudden cry. Wondering what it was, I turned to look in its direction and saw the dark elf looking at a letter, her face distorted with emotion. There was a white bird perched on her quivering shoulder.

Using a kui‚Äôs homing instinct and ability to pick up on waves emitted by its master at a long distance, it was possible to communicate between an individual and a fixed location. ‚ÄúWhat is it, Aisha?‚Äù Souma asked.

‚ÄúI think I‚Äôll be fine, but... Understood. You take care of yourself, too.‚Äù Liscia immediately ran off.

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs already been nearly half a day, then? The soonest we can arrive is two and a half days after the disaster... Having only half a day before we reach the 72 hour mark is going to be rough.‚Äù

Hal looked confused. ‚ÄúWhat‚Äôs that? What do you mean by ‚Äòthe 72 hour mark‚Äô?‚Äù

‚ÄúIn natural disasters like this, that‚Äôs the line after which the death rate for those in need of rescue shoots up. It‚Äôs three full days after the disaster strikes. It‚Äôs called the ‚Äò72-hour wall.‚Äô‚Äù

‚ÄúSorry. Could you say that in a way that‚Äôs easier to understand?‚Äù he asked.

‚ÄúIt means that a lot of lives can be saved in those 72 hours.‚Äù

‚ÄúI get it now... Wait, in that case, we can‚Äôt dawdle here! Shouldn‚Äôt we be getting our butts to the God-Protected Forest, pronto?! It‚Äôs gonna take a full two days, isn‚Äôt it?‚Äù he demanded.

‚ÄúI know that,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúDo we have a carriage?‚Äù

‚ÄúThe original plan only called for us to use carriages when we came here and when we left. If we need to get enough carriages for fifty people, that‚Äôs going to take time.‚Äù

‚ÄúDamn!‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúIs there no other way to move around...?‚Äù

I noticed something. Hal and the others looked to see what I was looking at, then gulped.

I was looking at the beasts pulling the container cars. If you take a rhino, add a Komodo dragon, divide by two, then multiply the size by ten, you would have these giant lizards, the rhinosauruses. They were big, but they could run continuously at high speeds comparable to a steam locomotive.

‚Äú...Hey, Hal, Kaede,‚Äù I said.

‚ÄúWhat?‚Äù Hal asked cautiously.

‚ÄúWhat is it?‚Äù Kaede asked.

‚ÄúIt‚Äôll probably make us all nauseous, so will you be okay?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúI‚Äôm quite resistant to motion sickness, you know,‚Äù Kaede said.

‚Äú...I‚Äôll deal with it,‚Äù Hal muttered.

‚ÄúYou will? I‚Äôll tough it out, too, then.‚Äù

I immediately gave the order to fifty members of the Forbidden Army.

‚ÄúUnload all the freight from the container cars! Fortunately, the road runs near the God-Protected Forest, but once we get into the woods, we‚Äôll be traveling on foot! The lighter our load, the better! Leave the materials where you unload them! Even if they‚Äôre lost, you won‚Äôt be blamed for it! I‚Äôll give a written apology to Hakuya and get off with a little scolding! Also, bring all the food with us! We can‚Äôt do something lame like show up to offer aid, then have to sponge off the locals for food!‚Äù

‚Äú‚Äú‚ÄúYes, sir!‚Äù‚Äù‚Äù

Following my orders, the Forbidden Army soldiers speedily unloaded the container cars.

As you might expect from people who‚Äôd been doing nothing but construction work, they moved fast. The way they efficiently worked together to carry off the materials made them look like skilled movers. They really did feel reliable.

‚ÄúNo, we‚Äôre soldiers, remember?‚Äù Hal complained.

‚ÄúStop prattling and get to work, Hal,‚Äù Kaede said.

Kaede was using her magic to easily move materials that would normally have taken a few big strong men working together to lift.

Earth magic was, in the end, the magic of gravity manipulation. It didn‚Äôt create earth or stone from nothing: it manipulated what already existed. That was probably why she could do tricks like this. It was a huge contribution.

...Right now, I was probably the least useful person here. Since I had below-average strength, even if I joined in with the soldiers, I would probably just be in the way.

As I stood there watching them work for lack of anything better to do, Aisha came up to me. ‚ÄúYour Majesty...‚Äù

She looked weak, as if she might break down at any moment.

Ever since I‚Äôd recruited her, Aisha had been at my side as a bodyguard, so I felt like I had seen a lot of her expressions. Her determined face when she made a direct appeal to me, her imposing warrior face, her childlike face when she was eating something, the face like an abandoned dog that she made when she had to wait for that food... I had seen many expressions from her, but this one was new.

To see a girl who was so much more powerful than me looking so weak pained my heart. Aisha was always protecting me as my bodyguard, but now it was time for me to protect her. I placed my hand atop her head, which was roughly the same height as mine.

‚ÄúS-Sire?‚Äù she asked.

‚ÄúLeave this to me.‚Äù I pulled her in, resting her forehead on my shoulder. ‚ÄúI have no power, and I‚Äôm far weaker that you, Aisha, but I‚Äôm in a position to make a lot of people move. So leave this to me. If there are lives that can be saved, I‚Äôll save all that I can.‚Äù

‚ÄúSire... Siiiiiiiiire!‚Äù Burying her face in my shoulder, Aisha began to cry.

I gently patted her head.

Until we were ready to go, I comforted the crying Aisha.

The God-Protected Forest was a forested area to the south of the country.

The name apparently came from the legend that a giant god-beast that took the form of a goat-antelope protected this forest.

That said, there had been no claimed sightings of it in recent years, and now the only proof of its existence was that its divine protection kept locusts from attacking the forest, kept droughts from drying it up, kept cold waves from freezing it, and kept the trees green at all times. This god-beast that only showed it existed through its divine protection... did it really exist?

The dark elves were the ones to claim their forest was under the god-beast‚Äôs protection.

The forest had to be approximately as big as the Sea of Trees around Mt. Fuji. They called it a forest, but it was actually the autonomous domain of the dark elves, and that xenophobic race had never let the other races enter their forest. Even Aisha had come to appeal to me for a crackdown on trespassers.

This time, there were close to fifty (hundreds once you considered the units to follow) humans coming to provide relief, and we would be entering the forest, but this was by request of the chief‚Äôs daughter, Aisha, so it would be treated as a special case, apparently. The dark elves lived in the forest, defended their independence, and hated outsiders.

As a matter of fact, despite the catastrophic landslide they had suffered, they apparently hadn‚Äôt sent a request for aid to the capital. If Aisha hadn‚Äôt been contacted, we might never have known the disaster had happened at all. It was admirable of them to try to solve their problems on their own, but it was stupid for them to let the number of deaths shoot up because of it.

‚ÄúThey‚Äôve become hardheaded because they don‚Äôt even try to look at the outside world,‚Äù Aisha spoke sadly as we walked through the God-Protected Forest. ‚ÄúBecause I made contact with you, sire, and you listened to my opinions, there were signs of that beginning to change, but...‚Äù

Her voice became indignant.

‚ÄúThis isn‚Äôt an era where we can live in the forest alone. With the threat of the Demon Lord‚Äôs Domain, we never know when they‚Äôll begin to move south! If we shut ourselves away in our forest, do they believe the god-beast will really save us when the time comes?! The god-beast is the protector of the forest, it‚Äôs not the protector of the dark elf race!‚Äù

‚ÄúY-Yeah...‚Äù I said, taken aback.

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs why we dark elves should study and learn about the wider world!‚Äù Aisha was impassioned. It felt like the first time she‚Äôd looked so respectable in a while.

‚ÄúBesides, if I stay in the forest, how would I eat Your Majesty‚Äôs delicious foods?!‚Äù she added.

...I take that back. Aisha was still Aisha.

Well, it‚Äôs better that she‚Äôs like this than to have her be tense and anxious, I thought.

Soon after we arrived in the dark elf village, we were met by a handsome man who looked to be in his twenties.

‚ÄúOh, Your Majesty!‚Äù he cried. ‚ÄúHow good of you to come.‚Äù

His handsome face bore a certain resemblance to Aisha‚Äôs. Could he be her big brother?

He was tall, probably at least 190 cm. I could tell from the accessories he wore on his head and arms that he was of a high rank, but the fine-looking robe he wore was covered in dirt. He looked a little tired, as well.

As she stood before that young elf, Aisha thumped her hand on her chest once. ‚ÄúFather, I have brought His Majesty here with me.‚Äù

‚ÄúWell done,‚Äù he said. ‚ÄúYour friendship with His Majesty must have come about through the guidance of our god-beast.‚Äù

‚ÄúFather?!‚Äù I exclaimed.

My surprise brought a smile to the young elf‚Äôs exhausted face.

‚ÄúMy king, it is a pleasure to meet you. I am the chief of the dark elves and Aisha‚Äôs father, Wodan Udgard. Thank you for taking such good care of my daughter.‚Äù

‚ÄúOh, sure. Um... You‚Äôre awfully young.‚Äù

‚ÄúPure-blooded elves stop aging once their bodies mature to a certain point,‚Äù he explained. ‚ÄúWe live three times longer than humans, too, so while I may look young, I‚Äôve still lived 80 years.‚Äù

I see, I thought. That‚Äôs about the same as the elves and dark elves you see in stories, huh? Those say that elves‚Äôre long-lived, stay youthful for a long time, and that they‚Äôre all beautiful. Though, my chamberlain, the half-elf Marx, was an old dude, wasn‚Äôt he? Do half-elves age differently, I wonder?

Setting that aside, I whispered to Aisha, ‚ÄúHe seems welcoming. I thought dark elves were supposed to be xenophobic?‚Äù

‚ÄúMy father is the head of the cultural liberalization faction, so he‚Äôs understanding of cultural exchange with the outside. Father was also the only one who approved of me going to make an appeal to you.‚Äù

‚ÄúI see. The reason you don‚Äôt worry about the rules is because of his influence, huh?‚Äù I said. I shook hands with Wodan. ‚ÄúI am the (acting) king, Souma Kazuya. I am here by the request of Aisha to provide relief.‚Äù

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs good of you to come,‚Äù he said. ‚ÄúAlso, you‚Äôre the king, so please, you don‚Äôt need to be so formal with me.‚Äù

‚Äú...Righty-o. Is this better?‚Äù

‚ÄúYes. Still, I never expected the king himself to come here.‚Äù

‚ÄúI happened to be doing an inspection at the time,‚Äù I explained. ‚ÄúI‚Äôve brought the fifty members of the Forbidden Army who were at hand as an advance party. A few days from now, a second group with relief supplies should arrive.‚Äù

‚ÄúI‚Äôm grateful. The truth is, I‚Äôd love to have the whole village come to welcome you, but given the circumstances, I hope you‚Äôll understand.‚Äù

‚ÄúI know,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúIt really is an awful situation.‚Äù

The dark elf village was in the center of a thick circle of warding trees. There were villages like this dotted around the forest, and the dark elves lived in them. If you were to look at the God-Protected Forest as a country, this village would be the capital, and there was an order of magnitude more dark elves living here than anywhere else.

The eastern third or so of that village had been carved away by the landslide. It looked like a slightly elevated slope on the eastern side had collapsed. Perhaps due to the long spell of rain, there was a large amount of water flowing over the exposed surface. The ground might have loosened a fair bit. Our one salvation was that it was sunny now. If it had been raining, we would have had to worry about another collapse while we worked.

‚ÄúWhat are the damages like?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúWe‚Äôve recorded nearly one hundred casualties already. There are still more than forty missing, as well.‚Äù

That‚Äôs a lot, I thought. It‚Äôs going to be a battle against time to see how many we can rescue.

‚ÄúLet‚Äôs begin the relief operation immediately,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúHowever, there‚Äôs a risk of secondary disasters, so it would be a good idea to have the women evacuate. Also, have some people keep an eye on the mountain, please. If the mountain moves in the slightest, or there are any weird noises, have them report it. If it were to collapse again while we‚Äôre carrying out relief operations, that would be a serious issue.‚Äù

‚ÄúI will do that at once,‚Äù he agreed. ‚ÄúIs there anything else you would like to ask of me?‚Äù

‚ÄúPlease compile a list of the missing. We‚Äôll erase them from it as we manage to ascertain their safety.‚Äù

‚ÄúUnderstood.‚Äù

Once I worked things out with Wodan, I gave orders to Aisha and the Forbidden Army.

‚ÄúAisha.‚Äù

‚ÄúYes, sir!‚Äù

‚ÄúHave the women evacuate to a place that doesn‚Äôt look like it will collapse. Consult with Wodan to decide where is best. You will escort them and ensure they‚Äôre delivered there safely.‚Äù

‚ÄúYes, sir! Understood!‚Äù

‚ÄúGood,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúStarting now, the Forbidden Army will begin operations to search for those whose safety is unconfirmed. You guys have a lot of skill at digging, I‚Äôm sure. Listen closely, and if you hear voices calling for help in the dirt, carefully rescue them!‚Äù

‚Äú‚Äú‚ÄúYes, sir!‚Äù‚Äù‚Äù

‚ÄúHowever, be absolutely sure that you don‚Äôt do anything you can‚Äôt handle. If it looks like there may be another collapse, retreat even if you‚Äôre in the middle of saving someone. The rescuers cannot be allowed to take even a single loss. Understood?‚Äù

‚Äú‚Äú‚ÄúYes, sir!‚Äù‚Äù‚Äù

Nodding at the Forbidden Army soldiers‚Äô response, I shouted an order. ‚ÄúWe will now commence relief operations!‚Äù

The relief effort was an all-out battle.

Everyone came together, doing everything they could. They called the names of the missing, listened closely, and if there was even the slightest response, they would carefully move the dirt and sand aside.

It didn‚Äôt matter who was a soldier and who was a man from the village, they worked together moving the earth and cutting apart fallen trees, then pulling out the people trapped underneath. Kaede was using her magic to move huge rocks, too, while the women from the village were feeding the displaced and tending to the wounded.

As for me, I had teamed up with Hal, and we were carrying out search operations.

‚ÄúHal, under that thick tree! Someone‚Äôs still breathing!‚Äù I called.

‚ÄúHuh?! I don‚Äôt hear any voice,‚Äù he said.

‚ÄúWell, they‚Äôre there! Just dig!‚Äù

Hal had a doubtful look on his face, but when he dug where I told him to, he found a little girl‚Äôs hand. ‚ÄúSeriously...? Just you wait, we‚Äôll have you safe soon!‚Äù

Hal moved the earth aside, pulling the dark elf girl out.

She already had brown skin, so it was hard to tell, but her complexion was looking bad. After being trapped in the moist earth for all this time, that was to be expected.

It was a good thing that the summer heat was still lingering. Were it a little later in autumn, she might have died from the cold while she‚Äôd been buried.

When I came back with a blanket, Hal was holding the girl and patting her on the back. ‚ÄúYou did well. You‚Äôre going to be okay now.‚Äù

‚Äú...Wah... Wahhhhhhhhhh!‚Äù

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs okay! You‚Äôre okay now!‚Äù Hal desperately tried to calm the wailing girl.

If you ask me, men are useless at times like this. Hal and I were both at a loss for what to do, just repeating ‚ÄúIt‚Äôs okay,‚Äù over and over.

I wrapped the girl in a blanket, waiting for her to calm down before calling over a nearby Forbidden Army soldier. ‚ÄúTake this girl to a safe place.‚Äù

‚ÄúYes, sir! As you command!‚Äù the soldier said.

Once we had seen the girl off, Hal said to me, ‚ÄúI‚Äôm amazed you knew she was there. I couldn‚Äôt hear her voice at all.‚Äù

‚ÄúEven while we‚Äôre talking, I‚Äôm searching,‚Äù I said.

‚ÄúDo you know some sort of searching spell?‚Äù he asked.

‚ÄúNot quite... This is what I‚Äôm using.‚Äù When I stretched my palm out to Hal, a little thing burrowed out of the ground and jumped up onto it.

Hal looked at it, blinking. ‚ÄúIs that... a mouse?‚Äù

‚ÄúA wooden one, yeah.‚Äù

It was a mouse carved out of wood, about 10 cm long. I had been manipulating it with my Living Poltergeists ability to search for survivors under the rubble. My ability was able to operate at long distances if I used dolls, but it seemed they only needed to be shaped like a living creature, not necessarily a humanoid one. Even as I was showing this one off to Hal, there were another four wooden mice moving around almost like real mice and looking for those in need of rescue.

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs a wonder that you were carrying around something like that,‚Äù he said.

‚ÄúI found them in a shop while I was on my date with Liscia,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúI thought I might use them for something, so I put them in the rolling bag with my other self-defense items.‚Äù

By the way, that bag had also held two small-sized Little Musashibo dolls which I now had on patrol in the area. Even in places where the landslide had damaged the roads, those lightweight little guys could jump around easily enough.

‚ÄúYour ability is more amazing than I‚Äôd ever have thought,‚Äù he said.

‚ÄúYeah. I feel like this is the first time outside of administrative tasks that I‚Äôve gotten some use out of... Urkh!‚Äù I crouched over and started vomiting.

‚ÄúWhoa, what‚Äôs this, out of nowhere?!‚Äù Hal called out to me, sounding concerned. ‚ÄúH-Hey, Souma.‚Äù

‚ÄúBlech...‚Äù I managed, then coughed violently.

‚ÄúA-Are you all right? Why‚Äôd you suddenly start puking?‚Äù

‚Äú...S-Sorry. While it was searching, one of my wooden mice... it suddenly found a really badly damaged body...‚Äù

‚ÄúDamaged...?‚Äù

‚ÄúThe eyeballs were‚Äî‚Äù

‚ÄúNo, stop! I don‚Äôt want to hear it!‚Äù Hal looked away and plugged his ears.

I looked at the dirt in front of us.

When the news covers disaster areas, they focus on the tragedies of the affected and the hopes of the survivors. However, now that I was actually experiencing it firsthand, it was a hell greater than I had imagined. This reality was too harsh for a general audience. It would break their hearts.

Still, I didn‚Äôt have time to be thinking about that.

‚ÄúHal! I‚Äôve found two people in need of rescue, in the shadow of a rock 50 meters ahead of us and to the left.‚Äù

‚ÄúOn it!‚Äù

‚ÄîFor now, I just had to kill my emotions.

We diligently continued with our relief efforts. We managed to dig a great many dark elves from the earth and rubble.

All of them were injured in one way or another, and many had serious injuries that couldn‚Äôt be taken lightly even once they had been rescued. Often, by the time we managed to dig them out, they had already expired.

At first, the ratio of living to dead among the rescued was half and half, but now it was leaning more heavily towards the dead. When I considered that, of the close-to-one-hundred casualties Wodan had mentioned when we had first arrived in the village, only two-tenths had been dead, it was clear that things were getting worse as time passed.

The searchers were showing signs of heavy exhaustion, as well. They had been resting in shifts, but it had now been three days since the disaster had occurred.

It had been hard on the dark elves, of course, but also on the soldiers who had come a long way and then spent a full day searching. They had already dug out a fair number of those in need of rescue (some alive, some not).

I thought it would be wise to check in with Wodan to confirm how many people were still missing. If we could narrow down the number of victims, we could focus our manpower on searching the area where we thought they would be.

As I was thinking that...

‚ÄúO Godbeast! Why have you let this happen?!‚Äù

...I heard a desperate cry.

When I looked, I saw a young (?) dark elf man who resembled Wodan wailing as he struck his fists and head against the ground.

Aisha had returned from evacuating the women and children, so I asked her about him. ‚ÄúAisha, who is that?‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs... my uncle, Robthor Udgard, He‚Äôs my father‚Äôs younger brother.‚Äù

‚ÄúFrom the way he‚Äôs crying and wailing, I guess that means...‚Äù

‚ÄúYes,‚Äù she confirmed. ‚ÄúHis wife and child, in other words my aunt and her daughter, have yet to be found.‚Äù

‚ÄúThat must be... difficult. Are you okay, Aisha?‚Äù

‚ÄúWell, you see... If my father is the head of the liberals, my uncle is head of the conservatives. I didn‚Äôt have much contact with them... His daughter was still young and cute, though, so it pains me to see this happen to her...‚Äù

‚ÄúI see...‚Äù

We were well past the 72 hour deadline. If she hadn‚Äôt been found yet, that meant...

Then, Robthor looked in our direction. When he saw us, he walked over towards us, stumbling as he did.

‚ÄúKing... O, king... Why?‚Äù

Robthor grabbed me by the lapels, causing Aisha to yell at him, but I motioned for her to stand down. Rather than gripping them tightly and trying to lift me up, he was just grasping at them, as if clinging to me. If I simply brushed him away, he would probably collapse.

‚ÄúO, king. I have done all I can to protect this forest. So why has it taken my family from me...?‚Äù

I was at a loss for words. I looked over to Aisha.

‚ÄúMy uncle opposed the periodic thinning,‚Äù she said. ‚ÄúHe said it was unthinkable that dark elves, as protectors of the forest, should cut down trees needlessly. The place that collapsed was one where we couldn‚Äôt do periodic thinning because of my uncle‚Äôs objections,‚Äù she explained.

That‚Äôs... I don‚Äôt know what to say...

‚ÄúO, king! Tell me why! Why would the forest I protected destroy my family? If I had cut down trees like Wodan and his lot, would my family have been spared?!‚Äù

‚ÄúThere‚Äôs... no way to know that,‚Äù I said.

‚ÄúNo!‚Äù he howled.

‚ÄúTrue, if you carry out periodic thinning, take care of the undergrowth, and increase the land‚Äôs ability to hold water, it‚Äôs possible to create conditions that reduce the likelihood of a landslide. However, it only makes it less likely. In a case like this, where heavy rain over a long period was the cause... It could have happened anywhere.‚Äù

‚ÄúNo... You‚Äôre saying we just had bad luck, then...‚Äù he murmured.

‚ÄúIn terms of where the landslide happened, yes. However, periodic thinning means there‚Äôs always work going on in the forest. The workers may hear strange noises, see the forest seeming to shift, and notice other warning signs that a landslide is about to occur. If they notice, there are things that can be done. People could have been evacuated.‚Äù

This has also been said to be an advantage of using mountains for terraced rice-fields.

You would think cutting down the trees to make room for rice paddies would make landslides more likely, but it actually reduces the odds of landslides that result in human casualties. Because people have to go into the fields all the time, they quickly notice the warning signs, and that makes it easy to respond. The strongest countermeasure against landslides is to watch the forest at all times. The elves didn‚Äôt have debris flow detection systems like in modern day Japan, so that made having people on watch all the more important.

‚ÄúI‚Äôve protected the forest all this time... was I wrong to do that?‚Äù he moaned.

‚ÄúYour belief that you were protecting the forest was wrong,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúNature‚Äôs not so fragile that it needs people to protect it.‚Äù

Aisha had told me before that the trees in the God-Protected Forest were long-lived. That was why they hadn‚Äôt noticed it had turned into a beansprout forest and the ground had been weakened. Even though they had simply been lucky that nothing had happened yet, they‚Äôd convinced themselves they were protecting the forest.

‚ÄúIf it‚Äôs egotistical for man to destroy the forest, so, too, is it egotistical to try to protect it,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúNature is meant to go through cycles of death and rebirth, yet we‚Äôre trying to keep it in a state that‚Äôs convenient for us. All people can do is manage things through periodic thinning, keeping the forest in a state where we can co-exist with it. Trying our best not to wake it from its slumber.‚Äù

He seemed speechless.

At that moment, one of my wooden mice discovered something.

‚ÄúThere! I found a parent and child!‚Äù I cried.

‚ÄúWh-Where?!‚Äù he stammered.

‚ÄúHold on... They‚Äôre in a collapsed house ahead and to the left of us, two meters from the mountain ridge!‚Äù

We rushed to the spot, moving the sand and dirt aside. When we did, we found a little girl and a woman I assumed was her mother in a gap between the collapsed lumber. The mother was holding her girl tightly, trying to protect her. When Robthor saw them, he let out a breathless sigh. Clearly, they were his wife and daughter.

When we pulled them out, the woman had already expired.

Just as I was thinking all hope was lost... Aisha raised her voice. ‚ÄúSire! The child is still breathing!‚Äù

‚ÄúGet her to the relief team, immediately!‚Äù I shouted. ‚ÄúDon‚Äôt let her die!‚Äù

‚ÄúUnderstood!‚Äù

After wrapping the child in a blanket and seeing her and Aisha off, I looked to Robthor, who was crying beside his wife‚Äôs body. I thought maybe I should let him be, but this man still had things he needed to protect. I couldn‚Äôt have him stopping here on me.

Placing a hand on his shoulder, I said quietly, ‚ÄúShe protected your daughter to the very end.‚Äù

‚Äú...Yes...‚Äù

‚ÄúPull yourself together! It‚Äôs your turn to do it now!‚Äù

He seemed startled. ‚ÄúYes... Yes...!‚Äù

Speaking through sobs, Robthor nodded again and again.

Some time after that, the second relief team that Liscia had gone back to call for arrived. With the search for all missing persons completed, the advance team was relieved of their duties.

For the reconstruction work, the more numerous and better-equipped second team would take over.

After offering one last silent prayer for the fallen, the advance team returned to the capital.
