The mud-covered and exhausted members of the advance team were packed into the container cars like frozen tuna about to be shipped out. Right about now, Hal was probably resting his head in Kaede‚Äôs lap and taking a good rest.

I was in a similar state myself, riding in the carriage with Liscia who had come to pick me up.

We had left Aisha behind in the village. With her homeland in that awful shape, there was no way she would have been able to focus on her duties. For the time being, I had told her to wait in the God-Protected Forest.

As I leaned against the window, dozing off...

‚ÄúI wasn‚Äôt able to do anything this time,‚Äù Liscia said sadly.

‚ÄúYou went to call a relief party, didn‚Äôt you?‚Äù I asked. ‚ÄúEveryone worked their very hardest. Actually... if there‚Äôs anyone who was unable to do anything, it was me.‚Äù

‚ÄúHardly. I hear you were a great help out there,‚Äù Liscia tried to reassure me, but I shook my head.

‚ÄúI‚Äôm the king. In times of crisis, giving commands in the field isn‚Äôt the king‚Äôs duty. A king‚Äôs duty is to prepare for a crisis before it happens. I... didn‚Äôt do enough of that.‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs not...‚Äù

‚ÄúI think the Forbidden Army worked well as a relief unit. Still, there were more places where I came up short. Means of communication, long-distance shipping, accumulation of aid supplies in each area, medical teams attached to the relief party, psychiatrists to treat patients with PTSD... I came up short on all of those things. Because I was so focused on the food crisis and the issue of the three dukes, I was lax in my preparations.‚Äù

I looked at my reflection in the window, covered in mud and wearing an expression of exhaustion.

Liscia was looking at me with concern, but I pretended not to notice.

Epilogue

The central city of the Carmine Duchy, Landel.

In the center of that central city, in the meeting room in Landel Castle, in the residing castle of Duke Georg Carmine, right now, the three dukes who controlled the land, sea, and air forces of this country had gathered.

First, at the head of the table was the lord of this castle, Georg Carmine.

This lion-faced beastman had a burly, muscular build that was apparent even through his military uniform. He had the appearance of a warrior who had weathered many battles. Beastmen were no longer-lived than humans, but even at the age of fifty, he showed no signs of decline. His very presence was enough to make the atmosphere tense.

Seated to Georg‚Äôs right was Admiral of the Navy, Excel Walter.

Wearing a kimono that was similar in style to the ones worn in Japan, she was a beautiful sea serpent woman with antlers poking through her blue hair. Sea serpents were a race that could live for over a thousand years, and she herself had already reached an age of more than five hundred, yet she still looked to be in no more than her mid-twenties. However, contrary to her appearance, her command showed all the experience that came with that age.

Sitting across from her was General of the Air Force, Castor Vargas.

He looked like a gallant young man, but the two oni-like horns that grew through his red hair, the membranous wings that grew from his back, and the lizard-like tail marked him as a half-dragon, a dragonewt. He was close to one hundred years old, but as a member of a race that lived to five hundred years, he was still treated as a youngster. He, too, looked like he was in a foul mood.

Looking at the other two, Excel sighed. ‚Äú...I was under the impression that we were meeting here to avoid a needless conflict.‚Äù

‚ÄúWhat, Duchess Excel, are you afraid of that whelp?‚Äù Castor took an aggressive tone with Excel. ‚ÄúHas the once-feared sea serpent Duchess Excel grown old?‚Äù

‚ÄúOh, me? And who was it who tried to seduce this old granny fifty years ago, hmm?‚Äù Excel asked.

‚ÄúUrkh.‚Äù

‚ÄúAlso, when you address me, it‚Äôs not ‚ÄòDuchess Excel,‚Äô it should be ‚ÄòMother,‚Äô shouldn‚Äôt it?‚Äù

‚Äú...Right.‚Äù

With that playful rebuttal, she deflated Castor.

In truth, Excel had been Castor‚Äôs first love. Perhaps because he had been unable to forget her even after his attempts failed magnificently, when he had later met Accela, her daughter who was closer to him in age, he had fallen in love with her at first sight and they had married. In short, Castor was Excel‚Äôs son-in-law. She was not someone he was in a position to argue with and win.

‚ÄúCastor, do you still mean to oppose the king?‚Äù she asked.

‚ÄúOf course! I don‚Äôt care if he‚Äôs a hero, or whatever else they want to call him, that fake king usurped the throne, forced Princess Liscia into a betrothal, and unjustly seized power in this country! How could I serve a guy like that?!‚Äù

‚ÄúThe only ones who tell it like that are the nobles being investigated for corruption,‚Äù she corrected him. ‚ÄúKing Albert abdicated of his own will in favor of the man he felt would be a better successor. The king‚Äôs relationship with Princess Liscia is close, too.‚Äù

‚ÄúI don‚Äôt know about that! He may just be making it look that way! If he wanted to rebuild this country, he could have done it as a vassal! Was there some problem with the former king‚Äôs reign?‚Äù he snapped.

Excel wisely said nothing.

There were no problems with it, but there were no good points to it, either, and that was a problem, thought Excel, but to say so would be too disrespectful to the former king, so she refrained.

Excel had found the speed with which Albert had abdicated dubious, but all signs since then had pointed to it being a wise decision. Excel didn‚Äôt remember Albert as a ruler who could make such a decision, but perhaps it merely meant he had grown as a person.

‚ÄúBesides, we three dukes have protected this country for many long years. I can‚Äôt stand the way he‚Äôs belittling us!‚Äù the man snapped. ‚ÄúThe letter he sent me as soon as the throne was abdicated to him was ‚ÄòServe me, or not, make your choice,‚Äô you know?‚Äù

‚ÄúIt was ‚ÄòIf you will cooperate with my reforms, I will provide food aid and build roads for you‚Äô... Right?‚Äù she asked.

The three duchies had a lower population than the crown demesne, and because they had armies to supply, they had reserves, so the food crisis had not been felt as deeply in them. However, when the food crisis had hit, the three duchies had opened up their reserves and begun rationing, so all of the merchants who‚Äôd dealt in foodstuffs had gone bankrupt due to lack of demand. Next, because of the rise in unemployment, shops had gone out of business because their wares wouldn‚Äôt sell. Then, in a chain reaction, the craftspeople who had supplied them had gone under, as well.

On that point, Souma had weathered the crisis by providing subsidies only to the poor, not distributing more than necessary, encouraging people to eat foods there had been no custom of eating before, and increasing the country‚Äôs transport capacity by building roads. In doing this, he had managed to minimize the degree to which the economy shrank. Furthermore, of the three duchies, only the Walter Duchy had independent maritime trade routes and had been able to just barely stop the negative feedback loop by selling off their excess merchandise to other countries.

But that‚Äôs something I was able to do because my duchy has a port city, Excel thought. Neither the Carmine Duchy nor the Vargas Duchy have inland trade routes. With his large army, along with the fleeing nobles and their personal retinues to care for, the Carmine Duchy must be suffering from serious economic problems. If that‚Äôs the case, why is Georg so adamant about opposing the king?

As she was thinking that, Castor roared, ‚Äú‚ÄòI‚Äôll feed you like a pet, so obey me,‚Äô is basically what that means! He‚Äôs looking down on us!‚Äù

‚ÄúIf it‚Äôs for the benefit of your people... what else is there to be done?‚Äù Excel asked.

‚ÄúI don‚Äôt like it! Does he think he can tame us with a little bait?!‚Äù

‚ÄúI doubt the king needs a pet with pride and little else,‚Äù Excel said.

Castor slammed both his hands down on the table. ‚Äú...What is with you today?! It‚Äôs like you‚Äôre defending the king! I know you don‚Äôt like him, either. That‚Äôs why you ignored the king‚Äôs requests for assistance!‚Äù

‚ÄúKindly don‚Äôt act as if we‚Äôre the same,‚Äù she said tartly. ‚ÄúWhat the sea serpent race must prioritize above all else is the peace and safety of our beloved Lagoon City. If he will just guarantee me that, I‚Äôm prepared to obey him.‚Äù

The sea serpent race, with Excel at their lead, had a unique system of values.

Sea serpents always thought of the needs of their city, Lagoon City, first and foremost. Their ancestors had once lived on an island in the Nine Headed Dragon Archipelago, but after losing in a power struggle within those islands, they had been driven out to sea, becoming wandering pirates.

Then, at the end of their long years of wandering, their ancestors had finally built a base of operations at what was now Lagoon City. The sea serpents protected themselves on this land which they had finally gained for themselves with love and with pride. The sole reason they had participated in the founding war of this multiracial state, the Elfrieden Kingdom, had been to protect Lagoon City.

‚ÄúIf it will benefit Lagoon City, I‚Äôll wag my tail for anyone, and if they threaten Lagoon City, I will eliminate them, no matter how great they are in number. That is the pride of the sea serpents,‚Äù Excel explained.

‚ÄúHmph, wagging your tail is something to take pride in?‚Äù he snorted.

‚ÄúYes. I fight to protect the things I must. I‚Äôm not an infant who throws a tantrum just because he doesn‚Äôt like someone. If it can be resolved by talking, there‚Äôs no better outcome than that. It would be absurd to start fighting among ourselves now, when our neighbors are eyeing us for an opportunity to strike.‚Äù

‚Äú...The Principality of Amidonia, huh?‚Äù he muttered.

He was referring to the country which bordered Elfrieden to the west.

When they had found themselves on the receiving end of the expansionist policies of the king who had been king before Albert, the Principality of Amidonia had lost close to half its land. Now, they were watching closely for any chance to regain their lost territory. Amidonia seemed eager to intervene in the dispute between King Souma and the three dukes, having already sent them a letter saying, ‚ÄúIf you intend to depose the false king, we are prepared to dispatch troops to aid you.‚Äù

‚ÄúHonestly, what a stubborn bunch,‚Äù he snorted. ‚ÄúTheir intentions are so transparent.‚Äù

‚ÄúI‚Äôm sure they‚Äôve sent a letter to the king, too,‚Äù Excel said. ‚ÄúI doubt the king will take them up on it, but they may dispatch ‚Äòreinforcements‚Äô anyway. You see what I mean? About how foolish it is for us to quarrel now.‚Äù

‚ÄúHmph. Fine, then why don‚Äôt you just go to the king‚Äôs side already.‚Äù

‚ÄúThere are a number of things I want to see and judge for myself, and then I plan to do just that. Things about the king, and about you.‚Äù

Excel turned a silent glance towards Georg Carmine. After some light pleasantries when she had first been brought into the room, he had closed his eyes and said nothing. Was he listening to Excel and Castor make their cases, or was he thinking about something himself? She didn‚Äôt think he was sleeping, but... Excel was beginning to become irritated with his demeanor.

‚ÄúGeorg, what are you thinking?‚Äù she snapped.

‚Äú...What do you mean, what?‚Äù

‚ÄúOh, my. So you were awake after all,‚Äù she said. ‚ÄúOf course I‚Äôm asking why you, the one who is most patriotic and loyal to this country of all of us, would take hostile actions against the new king.‚Äù

‚ÄúDuke Carmine, you don‚Äôt like that fake king either, right?‚Äù Castor demanded.

‚ÄúI wasn‚Äôt asking you, Castor,‚Äù Excel said. ‚ÄúAnswer me, Georg. Setting aside his legitimacy, his reign has been a stable one. Why would you go out of your way to cause turmoil like this?‚Äù

With Excel pressing him for answers, Georg opened his mouth gravely. ‚ÄúI judged him incapable of ruling this country. That is all.‚Äù

‚ÄúAnd why is that? What is it about his abilities, with which he will soon overcome the food crisis and economic difficulties that were pushing this country to the brink, that dissatisfies you?‚Äù

‚ÄúIn order to accomplish that, that king cast aside many things without hesitation.‚Äù Georg opened his eyes. That alone was enough to make the atmosphere in the room tense.

Excel and Castor both gulped. He was the youngest person present, yet in appearance and mentality, he was the most mature of all of them. This was the imposing presence of the greatest warrior in the country.

‚ÄúI‚Äôve heard that that king was summoned from another world,‚Äù he said. ‚ÄúBecause of that, he has no attachment to things and can discard them without hesitation. If he deems them inefficient, then be it history, traditions, soldiers, or vassals, he‚Äôll throw them away. Am I wrong, Duchess Excel?‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs...‚Äù Excel found herself at a loss for words. It was true, she could see that King Souma‚Äôs reign had that side to it.

‚ÄúVassals who‚Äôve served this country for many long years were abandoned by that king,‚Äù he continued.

‚ÄúYes, that was because they were corrupt.‚Äù

‚ÄúWill you still say that, even if they turn on him as a result? I believe you yourself just spoke of the folly of endangering the country at this time. That king is the one who sowed the seeds for it.‚Äù

‚ÄúYou say that, but you‚Äôre the one who‚Äôs sheltering those nobles,‚Äù she said.

‚ÄúThose with a grudge against the king will be useful pawns in defeating him,‚Äù he responded. ‚ÄúOf course, I have no intent of reinstating those people once the war is over.‚Äù

Excel shuddered at the way the corners of Georg‚Äôs mouth rose as he spoke those words. Does this man mean to work the corrupt nobles to death in a war?!

He would strike down the king, work the corrupt nobles to death, and even if he couldn‚Äôt dispose of all of them that way, he would find some excuse after the war to execute them. These were people for which any number of reasons could be found.

Then, with the current king‚Äôs faction and the corrupt nobles having vanished from the capital, only an empty lot on which he might build whatever he wished would remain. He could reinstate King Albert as his puppet, if he so wished. Or he could rise to become king himself.

Excel stood up. ‚ÄúHave you been driven mad with ambition for the throne?!‚Äù

‚ÄúH-Hey now, calm down,‚Äù Castor intervened, trying to smooth things over. ‚ÄúThis is Duke Carmine you‚Äôre talking about. I‚Äôm sure he‚Äôs not planning to usurp the throne, right?‚Äù

Georg gave a nod. ‚ÄúOf course not. Once King Souma is removed, I will have King Albert take the throne once more, and we will support him.‚Äù

‚Äú...I‚Äôm not convinced.‚Äù Excel lowered her posture. She was feigning calmness, but she was actually quite flustered.

The situation is worse than I anticipated. This is the worst possible scenario... Perhaps I need to act on the assumption that Georg already has undisclosed ties with Amidonia. Ugh, if Castor was any judge of character, we might have worked together to reign in Duke Carmine... Excel cursed her son-in-law for his short-sightedness.

Her daughter had married into his house and had since borne her two grandchildren. She was worried what might happen if she let Duke Carmine win, but if Excel were the only one to join the loyalist faction and King Souma were then to win, as the wife and children of the traitor Castor, what would become of Accela and her children? Under this country‚Äôs laws, when a serious offense was committed, relatives of up to three degrees of consanguinity were guilty of the same crime. If she cut ties with the House of Castor, the House of Walter would avoid that chain of responsibility, but if she did that, Accela and the children would...

‚ÄúCastor,‚Äù she said.

‚ÄúWhat?‚Äù

‚ÄúCut your ties with Accela, Carl, and Carla.‚Äù

‚ÄúAre you trying to say we‚Äôre going to lose to that whelp?!‚Äù he shouted.

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs in case the worst should happen. If you intend to face the king, at least be prepared for the possibility.‚Äù

Excel glanced over at Georg, but his eyes were closed, as if to say he had no intent of intervening. Even though she was discussing what would happen if he lost... Was this a show of confidence, perhaps?

Castor who had been asked to cut ties with his wife and children, on the other hand, had a troubled look on his face. ‚ÄúAccela and Carl, maybe... But Carla, I can‚Äôt.‚Äù

‚ÄúWhy not?!‚Äù Excel demanded.

‚Äú...Because she‚Äôll never listen to me.‚Äù

At that moment, the doors to the conference room slammed open.

Through the open door, a beautiful young girl entered. Her flaming red hair and shining golden eyes were quite distinctive. She was sixteen or seventeen years old. She wore heavy armor in a metallic red color, and from her back and rear protruded the wings and tail of a dragon.

‚ÄúCarla...‚Äù whispered Excel.

This was Castor‚Äôs daughter, Carla.

She had gotten her facial features from Excel and was a fair young beauty, but when it came to her temperament, Castor‚Äôs blood seemed to have won out. Instead of doing anything feminine, she had joined the air force unit led by Castor, training day in and day out.

Because of her beautiful face, many sons of the nobility and gentry had sought her attentions, but she had said in no uncertain terms that ‚ÄúI will never take a man weaker than me as my husband.‚Äù

In fact, she was the second strongest in the air force after Castor, and so she had handily trounced every one of her suitors. As a father, Castor was relieved, but as a parent, his feelings were more complicated, and he worried she might wait too long and never be able to get married.

Seeing Carla appear here, Excel had a bad feeling about what was going to happen.

And, as she had expected, Carla said, ‚ÄúGrandmother! If Father has decided to fight, then I shall fight, too!‚Äù

Excel shouted back, a vein pulsing on her forehead, ‚ÄúNo, you must not! Do you mean to become a traitor at your age?!‚Äù

‚ÄúI cannot forgive him for unseating King Albert and trying to force himself on my friend, Princess Liscia!‚Äù she declared. ‚ÄúI will punish him for his insolence personally!‚Äù

‚ÄúYou‚Äôve misunderstood!‚Äù Excel shouted. ‚ÄúKing Souma is...‚Äù

‚ÄúAh... It‚Äôs no use, Mother. Once she gets like this, Carla won‚Äôt budge an inch.‚Äù Castor shrugged his shoulders in resignation.

‚ÄúYou people... Honestly...‚Äù

Even as Excel held her head in consternation, Georg remained silent.

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

The capital of the Principality of Amidonia, Van.

In the territory of the Principality of Amidonia, which was longer on the map than it was wide, this city on the eastern side was the capital.

Some had felt it was too close to the Elfrieden Kingdom to be a capital, but its selection had likely been a manifestation of their unbroken determination to regain the stolen eastern territory.

In the governmental affairs office in the castle in the center of Van, a middle-aged man with a handlebar mustache was reviewing documents.

His cloaked figure looked somewhat plump, but this was only because he had broad shoulders. He was not actually obese. In fact, under his cloak, he was extremely muscular.

This man was Prince Gaius VIII of Amidonia.

‚ÄúOh ho...‚Äù he said.

‚ÄúWhat is it, Father?‚Äù A young man in his twenties who stood waiting at his side queried. He had a handsome face, but his eyes had a cold glint which chilled those who looked at them. He was the crown prince and heir apparent of the Principality of Amidonia, Julius Amidonia.

Gaius handed the document he had been reading to Julius. ‚ÄúIt‚Äôs from Georg Carmine. It seems he‚Äôs ready to ‚Äòstand up.‚Äô‚Äù

‚ÄúI see,‚Äù Julius said. ‚ÄúAt long last. I‚Äôve heard of the swift, severe attacks he would make in his younger years, never giving us time to catch our breaths. For a personage of such ability, he was awfully slow to act.‚Äù

‚ÄúHe‚Äôs grown old, I‚Äôm sure,‚Äù his father said. ‚ÄúWere his mind still keen, he never would have taken us up on our offer.‚Äù

‚ÄúTrue...‚Äù

After Julius returned the document to him, Gaius rose from his seat. ‚ÄúWe will move when the new king declares war. Send ‚Äòreinforcements‚Äô to the kingdom.‚Äù

‚ÄúOh...? And to which side?‚Äù

‚ÄúWhich? To the king‚Äôs side, we say, ‚ÄòWe are with the three dukes,‚Äô to the three dukes‚Äô side, we say, ‚ÄòWe are with the new king.‚Äô‚Äù

‚ÄúI see,‚Äù Julius said. ‚ÄúWe have no reason to obey either side that way.‚Äù

‚ÄúHeh heh heh. Precisely.‚Äù

Gaius and Julius looked to one another and shared a dark smile.

Beside them, there was a pair of cold eyes watching.

Good heavens... Sometimes I just ain‚Äôt sure what I oughta do about my old man and my idiot brother.

The cold eyes belonged to a young girl.

She was sixteen or seventeen years old. She had an attractive face, like Julius, but not his air of cruelty. If anything, her eyes were small and beady, and with her round face, she had the stuffed animal-like adorableness of a raccoon dog. Her hair was tied in two braids at the nape of her neck.

This girl who looked good in these braid-style twintails was the first princess of this country, Roroa Amidonia. However, contrary to appearances, her inner voice was sharp tongued (and spoke in mercantile dialect).

This country ain‚Äôt long for this world as is. Are these idiots tryin‚Äô to shorten what little time it has left? she thought.

Amidonia was a mountainous country. It had plentiful metal resources, but on the other hand, it had little arable land, so it was always faced with food shortages. The food crisis in neighboring Elfrieden was bad, but nothing compared to what this country faced. Even a slightly poor harvest would mean people starved to death.

I do understand why the old man‚Äôs tryin‚Äô to get even a little more fertile land for us, I do, but the old man‚Äôs pourin‚Äô every last cent that I worked so hard to scrimp and save for him into military fundin‚Äô. Roroa ground her back teeth together in frustration.

While Roroa was a princess, she also had uncanny financial sense, and she supported this country‚Äôs financial policies from the shadows. After getting the economy moving through foreign trade, she limited exports of resources and encouraged the export of finished products to protect and develop their industries. The reason this country on the brink hadn‚Äôt seen its economy collapse was in large part thanks to Roroa‚Äôs monetary sense.

However, Gaius had been unable to fully make use of Roroa‚Äôs money-raising ability.

If they‚Äôd been usin‚Äô the funds I‚Äôd earned to develop industry, they mighta been able to bring in even more funds, but these war mongerin‚Äô economic nitwits go and spend it all on the military. What makes it even worse is that they sincerely believe ‚ÄúIf we strengthen the military, we can steal whatever we need.‚Äù Are they morons? You spend money to make money, it‚Äôs that cycle that‚Äôs important. If you‚Äôre just dumpin‚Äô money into somethin‚Äô, that‚Äôs called wasteful spendin‚Äô! ...But even if I were to scream that at them, they probably wouldn‚Äôt listen to me...

‚ÄúYou agree, too, right, Roroa?‚Äù her brother said.

‚ÄúYes, Brother.‚Äù When the conversation suddenly turned to her, Roroa replied with a big fake smile. Though, in truth, she hadn‚Äôt been listening to a word they said...

...The end may finally be here for this country. Oh, how I envy the Elfrieden Kingdom. With their large population, they must have a lot of tax revenue they can move around, and best of all, their king‚Äôs the sort who‚Äôd be able to understand what I‚Äôm talkin‚Äô about. Honestly, I‚Äôm so jealous of our neighbor‚Äôs wallet... Their wallet?

At that moment, Roroa came to a realization.

If I‚Äôm jealous of my neighbor‚Äôs wallet... Why don‚Äôt I just combine it with my own? As legally as possible... Maybe I can do that? ...Yeah, maybe I can. In that case, I can contact the old man in charge of guarding Nelva...

Roroa began formulating a plan of her own. High risk, high return.

They say that as Roroa embarked on the greatest intrigue of her life, her smile resembled her father‚Äôs and brother‚Äôs just a little.

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

At the capital of the Elfrieden Kingdom, Parnam...

I was in the governmental affairs office in Parnam Castle, listening to the final report on the food crisis.

‚ÄúAs you see in the materials provided, we can expect good results from the fall harvest. Furthermore, the transportation network you laid out has accelerated the movement of people, and now goods have spread across the land without overabundance or shortages anywhere. Of course, this applies to foodstuffs, as well. From these facts, I believe we can treat the food crisis as, by and large, solved for now.‚Äù

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs good to hear,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúIt makes all the hard work worth it.‚Äù

It had been a long road, but now I could finally take a breath and relax. As the person who‚Äôd been grappling with this problem all this time, it was an especially emotional moment for me. However...

‚ÄúYes. With this, we can now safely move on to the next stage,‚Äù Hakuya said, with no regard whatsoever for my emotional moment.

...The next stage, huh.

‚ÄúWe... really have to do it, don‚Äôt we?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúDoes it weigh on you?‚Äù he asked.

‚ÄúWell, yeah. I understand the necessity of it, though...‚Äù

Yes. This was necessary.

The political theorist Machiavelli had said this in The Prince.

‚ÄúIf a prince should stain his hands with cruelties, even in peaceful times, he will have difficulty holding the state. However, for some tyrants, even after infinite cruelties, they live long and secure in their countries, defending themselves from external enemies and never being conspired against by their own citizens. I believe that this follows from cruelties being properly or badly used.

‚ÄúThose which may be called properly used are those applied in one blow at a time when it is necessary for one‚Äôs security. If a prince does not persist in them afterward, ruling in a way that advantages the people as best as he is able, he may even be remembered as a great ruler. However, one who fails to strike out the root of trouble from the beginning, dragging things out and inflicting repeated cruelties, uses them badly.‚Äù

This passage was one reason that Machiavelli‚Äôs The Prince had been, for a long time, criticized by the humanists of the Christian church. However, the cruelties he had spoken of there did not refer to massacres of ordinary people. He was talking about using trickery to permanently dispose of political opponents.

If you can stabilize your hold on power with one act of cruelty, then govern well afterward, it is a happy thing for the people. On the other hand, if you spend all your time worrying about what your political opponents think and don‚Äôt advance any worthwhile policies, not striking out the root of trouble in one blow, purging traitors again and again, you will lose the trust of the people.

The prince Machiavelli had held up as his ideal, Cesare Borgia, had massacred the influential nobles who had welcomed him during a feast, securing absolute power for himself.

Nobunaga Oda had used his severity well, taking the Oda Family from rural daimyos to becoming great daimyos in a single leap. However, in the end, because Nobunaga had persisted with his severities, he had shortened his own life, ultimately dying to a betrayal by one of his vassals.

In other words, ‚Äúcruelty‚Äù was like a prince‚Äôs treasured sword that could cut through anything, but if he grew addicted to using it, it was also like a cursed sword that would eventually destroy him.

‚ÄúAs I‚Äôve said before,‚Äù I said, ‚ÄúI‚Äôve deemed your plan a cruelty.‚Äù

‚ÄúYes,‚Äù he agreed. ‚ÄúYou also said, ‚ÄòIf we are to do it, let it be in one stroke.‚Äô‚Äù

‚ÄúYou can do it that way, I assume?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúThe preparations have already been made.‚Äù

‚Äú...Very well, then.‚Äù

I could say it was for this country, but I wasn‚Äôt that attached to the place.

I didn‚Äôt have a just cause, or a great one. But, when I questioned why I was doing it, suddenly Liscia and the others‚Äô faces came to mind. Those who lived, smiling, in this country: Liscia, Aisha, Juna, and Tomoe‚Äôs faces.

I thought of the bonds I had lost in the old world. I thought of the bonds I had formed in this new one.

I already thought of those girls as my family.

‚ÄúKazuya, build a family. And, once you have, protect them, come whatever may.‚Äù

...I know, Grandpa. I‚Äôll protect my family to the end, no matter what comes our way.

In order to do that, just this once, I will become a cruel king.

‚ÄúWe will now begin the subjugation.‚Äù

Extra Story: The Story of a Certain Group of Adventurers

Adventurers.

As the people who challenged and cleared out dungeons and the many mysteries that lay within, theirs was a profession filled with romanticized adventure. However, at the same time, they were also jacks and jills of all trades, taking quests issued by the guild (protecting merchants, slaying dangerous beasts, and more) in exchange for rewards. Now, here is something about these adventurers. Among the newest urban legends spreading in Parnam, the capital of Elfrieden, there is one known as...

‚ÄúThe Adventurer Who Wears a Kigurumi.‚Äù

It was said that this adventurer wore a kigurumi, a sort of full-body costume, that was 1.7 meters tall. His weapon was a naginata, slung over his back. He had a roly-poly body, but was able to move quickly and was apparently very talented. He formed no party, taking on dangerous beast subjugation quests solo, but occasionally, if there was a party seeking temporary members, he would join them for a dungeon crawl.

Incidentally, his name was registered with the guild as ‚ÄúLittle Musashibo.‚Äù

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

‚ÄúUh... So, you‚Äôre the adventurer who‚Äôs temporarily joining our party?‚Äù a male warrior asked doubtfully.

A roly-poly kigurumi was standing in front of the quest board in the guild. It stood before a party of four adventurers (party composition: one male warrior, one male priest, one female thief, and one female mage).

In the kigurumi‚Äôs hands was a naginata, on his back a wicker basket, his face was covered with white silk (in fact, it was sewn on), and the acorn eyes and bushy eyebrows that peered out from it were adorable.

Who was that? Was he a snowman? Was he a round-bottomed doll? No, he was Little Musashibo!

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo waved his arms around wildly, meaning, ‚ÄúThat‚Äôs right.‚Äù)

‚ÄúOh, could it be that you‚Äôre the kigurumi adventurer people have been talking about lately...?‚Äù Dece asked. He was a male swordsman with an attractive face that wouldn‚Äôt have been out of place in a boy band.

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo nodded.)

‚ÄúA-Are you now...?‚Äù Dece‚Äôs expression became a little strained.

Considering Little Musashibo‚Äôs silly appearance, that reaction was only to be expected. The rest of his comrades were bewildered, too.

‚ÄúOh, come on, I know we‚Äôre short a person on the front line, but does that really mean we need to bring in a guy like this?‚Äù demanded a beautiful young girl whose defiant eyes left a strong impression. Her voice was full of venom. This girl with a slightly punk sense of fashion was the female thief, Juno. The adventurers called thieves were, of course, not actual robbers. It was a support role in the party that detected enemies and disabled traps in the dungeon and could handle melee combat, as well.

The kindly-looking male priest, Febral, rebuked her. ‚ÄúW-Well, his outfit may be ridiculous, but everything I‚Äôve heard indicates he‚Äôs a reliable adventurer. I don‚Äôt think there should be an issue. We aren‚Äôt delving into a dungeon today, and the difficulty for this is supposed to be beginner level anyway.‚Äù

His role as priest was also just what people called a healer. It didn‚Äôt indicate any sort of religious belief.

‚ÄúOh, sure, what‚Äôs the harmmm? He‚Äôs kinda cute, anywayyy!‚Äù This light and airy beauty, the female mage Julia, started to playfully lean against Little Musashibo, enjoying his softness. Little Musashibo acted a little annoyed by this.

With a dry laugh at the scene, Dece extended his hand to Little Musashibo. ‚ÄúAnyway, it‚Äôll be a pleasure to work with you today.‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo shook his hand.)

‚Äú...Are you not able to talk?‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo nodded.)

Dece said nothing for a moment. Then he burst out, ‚ÄúOh, come on, is this really going to be all right?‚Äù

There was no one who could answer Juno‚Äôs doubts.

With Little Musashibo joining them, the party headed for an underground passage in the capital.

Apparently, these tunnels had been originally created to let the royal family escape in the event that an enemy attack reached the capital. Because of that, in order to confound intruders, the passages had been built as a complex maze with three levels.

On this occasion, the adventurers had received a quest calling for ‚ÄúExploration of the underground passages and investigation of creatures living therein (and if possible, their removal).‚Äù

Because this country had been free of war and chaos since the time of the former king, King Albert, the importance of these tunnels had diminished and they were no longer being properly maintained. As a result, giant rats and other such massive creatures had soon made their home in them. With the situation inside the tunnels at this point, it wouldn‚Äôt have been out of place to call them a dungeon.

Now, here was the thing about those underground tunnels. Apparently the recently-enthroned king wanted to repurpose them, and had posted this quest with the guild for that reason. Until the underground passages were safe and secure, any number of people were welcome to challenge it. The reward paid would be dependent on the creatures hunted. It was a low risk, low reward quest suited to beginners.

The adventuring party, now with the addition of Little Musashibo, was progressing through those underground tunnels. In the cold, wet air, an irritated Juno poked Little Musashibo‚Äôs head.

‚ÄúHey, don‚Äôt let this guy stand in front! He‚Äôs blocking my line of sight.‚Äù

‚ÄúHaving a front-liner stay in the back would be pointless,‚Äù Dece snapped. ‚ÄúDeal with it.‚Äù

With Dece telling her off, Juno clicked her tongue in displeasure. That was when it happened.

A giant snake appeared suddenly before the adventurers. The snake was ten meters long and thick enough to wrap one‚Äôs arms around. It raised its head, hissing menacingly at the adventurers. Immediately, Dece and Musashibo moved up.

‚ÄúWe‚Äôll handle the front line! Everyone else, support us from the rear!‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo gave a thumbs up.)

In the next moment, the giant snake struck. It went for Dece. From there on, the snake ignored Little Musashibo for some reason, only trying to attack Dece.

‚ÄúWait, why‚Äôs it only going for me?!‚Äù Dece cried.

‚Äú?!‚Äù (Little Musashibo was confused.)

Allow me to explain. Because snakes search for their prey by detecting their body heat, it could not detect anything from Little Musashibo, which was just a kigurumi.

Dece took a tail slap from the giant snake and, while he did manage to block it with his shield, was thrown off balance. Taking advantage of the opening, the snake slithered between the two of them, attacking the three people in back. The first to be targeted was Juno, who had been acting as support in the middle guard.

‚ÄúWhoa, why‚Äôs it ignoring that kigurumi and coming at me?! I‚Äî I can‚Äôt stand snaaaaakes!‚Äù

It seemed that the sudden snake attack had made Juno‚Äôs legs give out. With her falling on her rump and unable to move, the snake opened its mouth wide and came at Juno. At that moment, just when she was sure she was going to die...

Slash!

Just as the snake was about to sink its fangs into Juno, Little Musashibo used his naginata to cut it clean in two from behind. With a cut in the middle severing its head from its tail, both halves of the snake continued to thrash about for a while before eventually falling silent.

Little Musashibo swung his naginata to clean the blood from it.

Having regained her senses, Juno shyly said to Little Musashibo, ‚ÄúTh-Thanks...‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo gave her a thumbs up and then patted Juno on the head.)

When she saw Little Musashibo not boasting, but showing concern for her instead, Juno brought a hand to her chest. She must have been terribly frightened, she thought, because her heart was racing for some strange reason.

H-He‚Äôs a weirdo... but he‚Äôs not a bad guy, it seems.

Having reevaluated her opinion of the man (?), Juno chased after the rest of the party.

The party continued their exploration. When they entered the second level, the attacks by giant creatures only became more intense. Now they weren‚Äôt only facing single enemies; some attacked in packs.

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo cut down a swarm of giant bats with a whirlwind attack.)

‚ÄúOh, you‚Äôre pretty good.‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo gave Dece a thumbs up.)

‚Äú...Hm? Hey, pal...‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo tilted his head to the side, as if to say, ‚ÄúWhat?‚Äù)

‚ÄúThere‚Äôre a number of little bats hanging off your back, you know...‚Äù Dece said.

‚Äú?!‚Äù (Little Musashibo flailed around.)

‚ÄúYeesh... Here, I‚Äôll get them for you,‚Äù said Dece.

Allow me to explain. Little Musashibo had no sense of pain, and therefore hadn‚Äôt noticed he was getting bitten.

‚ÄîA few minutes later.

Splish, splash.

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo had fallen into a hole full of water and was thrashing around.)

Splish, splash.

‚Äú...‚Äù (‚ÄúHurry, help me,‚Äù he appealed to the party members.)

The sight made Julia and Febral feel warm and fuzzy inside.

‚ÄúHe looks like he‚Äôs playing around...‚Äù said Julia.

‚ÄúHe does,‚Äù Febral agreed.

‚ÄúHey, let‚Äôs hurry and help him!‚Äù Juno said. ‚ÄúCome on, you too. Grab a hold already.‚Äù

Juno reached out, pulling Little Musashibo up. Having been rescued, Little Musashibo bowed to Juno again and again.

‚Äú...‚Äù (‚ÄúThank you so much! I will never forget your kindness!‚Äù he was saying.)

‚ÄúY-You don‚Äôt need to thank me,‚Äù Juno stammered. ‚ÄúI owed you for before. It‚Äôs only natural for comrades to help one another.‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (‚ÄúYou‚Äôre willing to recognize me as a comrade?!‚Äù He was overcome with emotion.)

‚ÄúWh-Who cares! Come on, let‚Äôs go already.‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (‚ÄúAh, wait for me!‚Äù He chased after Juno.)

Little Musashibo‚Äôs slow, easy footsteps faded into the distance. The remaining members of the party were dumbfounded.

‚ÄúJuno... Was she just talking with that kigurumi?‚Äù Dece asked.

‚ÄúThat was what it looked like to me,‚Äù Febral nodded. ‚ÄúThe kigurumi didn‚Äôt say anything, though.‚Äù

Julia giggled. ‚ÄúIf she was, it may have been the power of love...‚Äù

‚Äú‚ÄúLove?!‚Äù‚Äù The two men‚Äôs simultaneous response echoed through the dark tunnel.

‚ÄîA few more hours later, the adventurers finally reached the third level.

Perhaps it had been built to be spacious, because the ceilings looked to be twenty meters high, and the paths were wide. This third level was the lowest in these underground passages. Though there had been some little mishaps along the way, their progress down here had been nothing if not smooth.

‚ÄúThis is no challenge,‚Äù Juno said. ‚ÄúI can see why they said it was beginner level.‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo cocked his head to the side as if to say, ‚ÄúReally?‚Äù)

‚ÄúWe‚Äôre used to the monsters in dungeons, see,‚Äù Juno explained. ‚ÄúNo matter how ferocious they are, we‚Äôre not going to lose to some animals.‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (He looked at her as if to say, ‚ÄúYou say that, but you were awful scared of that snake...‚Äù)

‚ÄúTh-That one doesn‚Äôt count! Everyone has things they‚Äôre afraid of!‚Äù Juno burst out.

‚Äú...‚Äù (He shrugged his shoulders as if saying, ‚ÄúSure, sure, I get it.‚Äù)

‚ÄúHey, if you‚Äôve got something to say, say it!‚Äù she fumed. ‚ÄúIf I got serious...‚Äù

The rest of the party looked on dumbfounded as the two argued back and forth in the underground tunnel. (Though Juno was the only one talking.)

‚ÄúSeriously, how is that conversation working?‚Äù Dece asked.

‚ÄúI am inclined to start believing Julia‚Äôs suggestion of ‚Äòlove,‚Äô‚Äù Febral said.

Then, it happened.

‚ÄúHuh?! Everyone, be on your guard!‚Äù Juno shouted.

The relaxed atmosphere was blown away, and everyone got into position for battle. The way they could do this like flipping a switch was part of what made adventurers so impressive.

Dece asked, ‚ÄúJuno, how many are there?‚Äù

‚ÄúOne,‚Äù she answered. ‚ÄúBut it‚Äôs unbelievably huge.‚Äù

Thieves had sharp senses and could use the slightest sound or vibration to judge the precise number and size of opponents in another location.

‚ÄúHow big‚Äôre we talking here?‚Äù Dece asked.

‚ÄúThat giant snake was nothing in comparison,‚Äù she replied.

‚ÄúThis is just an underground passage, right?‚Äù Julia asked. ‚ÄúWhy is there something so big here?‚Äù

Febral was the one to answer. ‚ÄúI‚Äôve heard that, in underground spaces like this, creatures can grow to sizes that would be unthinkable under normal circumstances. Once they reach a certain size, they have no natural predators and, because temperatures stay about the same here year-round, rather than die, they just keep growing bigger.‚Äù

‚ÄúSo, you‚Äôre saying there‚Äôs one up ahead that got big like that?‚Äù Dece asked.

The moment those words left Dece‚Äôs mouth, the air shook. It didn‚Äôt take a thief‚Äôs skills to know that the massive whatever-it-was was almost upon them.

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs coming!‚Äù Juno shouted.

The creature appeared. Its massive body nearly reached the ceiling, which was already high for an underground tunnel. It had slimy skin, and, unlike its mouth which looked like it could open big and wide, its eyes were so small they didn‚Äôt realize they were eyes at first.

‚Äú‚Äú‚Äú‚ÄúA salamander!‚Äù‚Äù‚Äù‚Äù the four shouted in unison.

Only one person (?), Little Musashibo, said, ‚Äú...‚Äù (‚ÄúA ridiculously huge salamander?!‚Äù), having a different reaction from the rest.

Dece couldn‚Äôt believe his eyes. ‚ÄúOh, come on... Normally salamanders are maybe two meters long, at most, you know?‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (‚ÄúThis world‚Äôs salamanders are usually the size of Komodo dragons?!‚Äù) Little Musashibo was surprised, but nobody was able to notice.

‚ÄúThis one looks like it‚Äôs clearly more than ten meters long,‚Äù Dece said.

‚ÄúSo they can grow to become this large...‚Äù Febral sounded impressed. ‚ÄúHowever, it is an issue that it‚Äôs a salamander. Their mucus is highly acidic. It would be dangerous to attack with melee weapons, and it‚Äôs resistant to heat. On the other hand, if we can freeze it, this could be an easy fight...‚Äù

‚ÄúWe don‚Äôt have anyone who can use ice magic,‚Äù Dece said. ‚ÄúIf flames worked, Julia could‚Äôve handled it with her magic, but... How about you, Mr. Kigurumi?‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (‚ÄúNuh uh.‚Äù He shook his head.)

‚ÄúWell, there‚Äôs nothing else for it, then. ...Let‚Äôs run,‚Äù said Dece, the party leader, calling for a retreat. ‚ÄúOur quest was to explore and investigate. There‚Äôs no need to overextend ourselves. If we just report that we found that thing, the castle ought to be able to send out a subjugation team later.‚Äù

‚Äú...I get what you‚Äôre saying, but can we get away so easily?‚Äù Febral asked.

As Febral pointed out, the salamander had the adventurers firmly in its sights.

Dece ground his back teeth, bringing up his shield and moving forward. ‚ÄúWe‚Äôll have to get away. Febral and Julia are fastest, so they go first. Juno doesn‚Äôt have a lot of gear, so she can go next. Mr. Kigurumi, can I count on you to bring up the rear with me?‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (‚ÄúOkie-dokie!‚Äù He gave a thumbs-up.)

‚ÄúOkay... Split!‚Äù

They all moved when Dece gave the order.

Febral and Julia ran back along the path they had come from, while Dece and Little Musashibo stayed behind, keeping the salamander in check. Juno put her legs to good use, running around nimbly and confusing the salamander. The salamander tried to go after the two that fled but, with Dece and Little Musashibo blocking it and Juno‚Äôs movements leaving it bewildered, it couldn‚Äôt make much progress forward.

Eventually, it must have gotten impatient, because the salamander let out a cry and swung its long tail. When it did, the mucus that had been attached to its tail flew everywhere.

‚ÄúOh, shoot! Everyone, look out!‚Äù Dece shouted.

‚ÄúEek!‚Äù Julia screamed.

The highly acidic mucus rained down and struck the adventurers. It stuck to Dece‚Äôs shield, Juno‚Äôs breastplate, the back of Febral‚Äôs vestments, and Julia‚Äôs long skirt, hissing and releasing an unpleasant smell as it dissolved the cloth and metal.

‚ÄúSalamander mucus will melt flesh, too! Strip off any equipment it got on!‚Äù Febral shouted as he pulled off his top.

When they heard that, Dece dropped his shield and Julia stripped off her skirt, continuing to run with her underwear showing.

‚ÄúHold on, it got my breastplate!‚Äù Juno shouted.

‚ÄúWell, hurry up and take it off! If you don‚Äôt, forget your breasts, you‚Äôll be showing your bare ribs instead!‚Äù Dece shouted.

‚ÄúUrgh...‚Äù

With Dece shouting at her, Juno stripped off her breastplate and shirt, going topless. She did her best to cover herself with her right arm while holding her short sword ready in her left, but she was turning bright red from embarrassment.

‚ÄúJuno, just go already! Mr. Kigurumi, are you all right?‚Äù

Once Dece confirmed that Juno had started running, he looked over to Little Musashibo to find its face was covered in mucus.

‚ÄúH-Hey! What‚Äôre you doing?! Take off that kigurumi already!‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù

Despite Dece‚Äôs worries, Little Musashibo shook his head back and forth. On a closer look, while he did have mucus on him, there was no sign of any melting.

‚Äú...Hold on, is your kigurumi acid resistant?‚Äù Dece asked.

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo gave him a thumbs-up.)

Allow me to explain. For Little Musashibo‚Äôs ‚Äúskin,‚Äù his well-paid creator had used his wages liberally, having nothing else to spend them on, and so it was made of special, high-quality, bladeproof, bulletproof, cold-resistant, heat-resistant, acid-resistant fibers.

For a moment, Dece was struck dumb. ‚ÄúHa ha ha...! Okay, in another ten seconds, we‚Äôll run, too. Get ready... Three, two, one.‚Äù

On the count of one, both of them turned on their heels and ran off. The salamander gave chase. However, perhaps due to the size of its massive body, it wasn‚Äôt very fast.

Just as they were thinking We may be able to escape! ...the salamander swung its tail once more. Because it did it while running this time, the mucus splattered all over in random directions.

‚ÄúUgh!‚Äù Juno howled.

‚ÄúJuno!‚Äù Dece shouted.

The mucus didn‚Äôt hit Dece or Musashi, but unfortunately it did graze Juno‚Äôs leg. Juno crouched down, holding her leg tight. It looked like she couldn‚Äôt move through the extreme pain. At this rate, it was going to catch up to them. That was when...

‚Äú...!‚Äù (Little Musashibo ran forward.)

‚ÄúUwah!‚Äù Juno yelped.

...Little Musashibo lifted her up in his arms, throwing her into the wicker basket on his back. Then, with Juno still in the basket, Little Musashibo ran off with slow, easy steps. Juno poked her head out of the basket, looking at Little Musashibo‚Äôs face in profile as he ran.

‚ÄúUh, um... Thanks.‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo gave her a thumbs-up.)

Then, just in the nick of time, Dece and Little Musashibo ran through a narrow hole.

Having made the difficult escape from the salamander and returned to the surface, the adventurers made their report to the guild. While they hadn‚Äôt succeeded in slaying the salamander, their sighting report was deemed valid, and they were paid a hefty sum for it. It sounded like a subjugation force would be dispatched to deal with that salamander soon. Regardless, the quest was now complete.

With their reward in hand, the party set out to divide the spoils among themselves. However, for whatever reason, Little Musashibo made no attempt to take any for himself. Dece was at a loss for what to do.

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs not fair, we owe you for saving Juno! Please, take your reward,‚Äù Dece pleaded.

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo silently shook his head.)

‚ÄúAre you really, really sure you don‚Äôt want any?‚Äù

‚Äú...‚Äù (Little Musashibo nodded. Then he waved, ‚ÄúGoodbye.‚Äù)

Little Musashibo walked away from the party with slow, easy footsteps. Julia and Juno, who had already changed into fresh clothes, watched that man (?) go with bewildered looks on their faces.

‚ÄúI wonder, what was that person (?) really?‚Äù Julia asked.

‚ÄúDon‚Äôt ask me,‚Äù Juno said. ‚ÄúWas that thing even a person?‚Äù

‚ÄúI‚Äôll bet there was a little fairy insiiiide...‚Äù Julia teased.

‚ÄúI doubt it,‚Äù Juno said. ‚ÄúBut, if there was... I‚Äôm sure...‚Äù

I‚Äôm sure it was a good fairy, thought Juno.

Little Musashibo departed, leaving behind only a mystery. Was the mage right, and was he a fairy?

And thus, another urban legend was born in the capital.

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

Within the large communal bath inside Parnam Castle...

In here there was the torso of a large-sized Little Musashibo soaking in a tub, Souma who was washing the acid and mud off of it, and Liscia who was watching him with a cold look in her eyes.

‚Äú...Is it just my imagination, or is it even bigger than when I saw it last time?‚Äù she demanded.

‚ÄúThat was a prototype,‚Äù he explained. ‚ÄúI used it as a model when I sent out the job request to craftsmen in the castle town.‚Äù

‚ÄúAh! Don‚Äôt tell me the ‚ÄòKigurumi Adventurer‚Äô they‚Äôre talking about all over town is...‚Äù

‚ÄúYeah, it‚Äôs probably this guy... Wait, Liscia? Why the scary look?‚Äù

‚ÄúFirst the mannequin, now this! Are you trying to convince people that Parnam is the demon capital?!‚Äù she shouted.

‚ÄúOw, that hurts...! Wait, whoa!‚Äù

When Liscia threw a bucket at him, Souma ended up diving, clothes still on, into a cold water bath. While in the water, Souma thought back on everything Little Musashibo had experienced today.

I never would have imagined there was a giant creature like that under the capital. I‚Äôm glad we were able to find it before damage reports started to come in, but I put Juno and her friends in danger...

He had optimistically assumed that even novice adventurers ought to be able to handle the wild animals living in there, so he had messed up and set the difficulty level too low. It had nearly meant adventurers dying needlessly on a quest that he himself had set. The reason he hadn‚Äôt taken the reward at the end was that he felt it was the least he could do after the trouble he‚Äôd caused Juno and the others.

...Though the biggest reason was that it would be wrong to accept the reward for a quest he set himself.

Regardless, I really do have to reflect on what happened today. Though...

‚ÄúUh, um... Thanks,‚Äù Juno had said.

When he recalled Juno‚Äôs face when she shyly said that as Little Musashibo carried her, the corners of Souma‚Äôs mouth naturally rose a little.

...The adventure itself was fun. I hope I‚Äôll get the chance to do it again.

That was what Souma thought as he sat there soaking in the dirty water.

Bonus Short Stories

The Little Tanuki Princess of Amidonia

The capital of the Principality of Amidonia, Van.

As might be expected from a nation of warriors, the city was surrounded by high walls and the buildings were ashen gray, free of excessive stylistic flourish. Perhaps because their ruler‚Äôs focus leaned so strongly towards the military, the layout of the city was a convoluted mess full of alleyways.

Right now, a young girl was running through those alleyways. She was sixteen years old, perhaps, with a petite, slender physique. Her face had regular features and she tied her hair back in twin braids.

This was the daughter of current Sovereign Prince Gaius VIII, Roroa Amidonia.

She had an air about her that was different from her stern and austere father Gaius or her coldly calculating brother Julius. The way she was curious about anything and everything made her as adorable as a little animal.

When she went out into the city, people were always quick to call out to her.

‚ÄúOh my, it‚Äôs little Roroa. Hello there,‚Äù a woman said, to Roroa, preparing to open up shop.

‚ÄúHello, Ma‚Äôam. Turnin‚Äô a nice profit?‚Äù

‚ÄúNot at all. The economy‚Äôs poor everywhere.‚Äù

‚ÄúI see. Sorry ‚Äòbout that. My stupid old man‚Äôs not so good at governin‚Äô.‚Äù

‚Äú...You must be the only one in this country who could say that,‚Äù the woman said with a strained smile. As was not uncommon in militaristic states, any criticism of those in power would quickly get a person arrested here. The only reason Roroa could get away with talking the way she did was because she was the first princess of this country.

However, Roroa replied with a smile that didn‚Äôt feel at all like it came from a princess.

‚ÄúJust you wait. I‚Äôll do somethin‚Äô about it.‚Äù

‚ÄúHahaha, I‚Äôll look forward to that.‚Äù

‚ÄúSure!‚Äù

With a wave to the woman, Roroa ran off again.

On the shopping street in Van, there was a store that dealt in men‚Äôs apparel. The little sign out front read ‚ÄúThe Silver Deer‚Äù in a stylish font. Roroa opened the door to the Silver Deer with great force, calling loudly to the owner.

‚ÄúSeeeebastiaaaan~‚ô™ Leeeet‚Äôs plaaaay~‚ô™‚Äù

‚Äú...Lady Roroa.‚Äù

When she did, a middle-aged man with graying hair who was dressed like a bartender came out. He seemed like the sort of stylish and deep-thinking man who the aroma of black tea would suit well, but he was holding his head, as if suddenly afflicted with a headache.

‚ÄúDon‚Äôt shout people‚Äôs names so loudly. What do you mean, let‚Äôs play?‚Äù

‚ÄúGeez, you‚Äôre no fun, Sebas.‚Äù

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs Sebastian, and I‚Äôm working right now...‚Äù

‚ÄúHmm? I didn‚Äôt get the feelin‚Äô you had any customers.‚Äù

Roroa looked around the store, but she didn‚Äôt see any customers. The store had a nice atmosphere to it, and many of the items on display were tasteful, so it was strange to see business so dead.

‚Äú...Well, the men of Van never were much for fashion,‚Äù Sebastian said with a wry laugh.

The Silver Deer had branch stores around Amidonia, but despite the store in Van being the head office, its sales were terrible. Given the austere ruggedness that was the national character, men in Amidonia didn‚Äôt concern themselves with what they wore, and this trend was especially pronounced in Van.

‚ÄúNormally, it‚Äôd be women who‚Äôd go for stylish stuff like this, though.‚Äù

‚ÄúThe day I start to stock stylish clothes for women is the day this store goes under.‚Äù

In the patriarchal society of Amidonia, women were looked on with disdain if they were seen walking outside in needlessly showy attire. That was why Amidonian women only wore clothing in subdued colors, so even if this store were to stock stylish clothing for women, it wouldn‚Äôt sell at all.

This was another thing that Roroa was dissatisfied about.

‚ÄúHonestly, it‚Äôs stupid. The market is defined by customer demand. Expandin‚Äô the market‚Äôs what leads to economic development, but our society‚Äôs placin‚Äô limitations on customer demand.‚Äù

While Roroa was a princess, she also had a rare sense for economics. Together with people like Colbert, the Minister of Finance, she had been moving around the country‚Äôs financial capital to make a profit and enrich the country. However, her father Gaius spent most of that profit almost entirely on expanding the military.

‚ÄúReally, if I want to rebuild this country, maybe I‚Äôll have to level everythin‚Äô first. That would take the fixed ideas people have got into their heads and blow them all away.‚Äù

‚ÄúHonestly... Could you not say such dangerous sounding things in my establishment?‚Äù Sebastian said with a sigh of dismay.

‚ÄúSo, Lady Roroa, how may I be of service today?‚Äù

‚ÄúHm? Oh, right. I wanted to ask you about somethin‚Äô.‚Äù

As Roroa said this, she edged up to Sebastian like a needy kitten. In these sorts of gestures, she really was like a small animal.

‚ÄúListen, are you connected to merchants outside the country, Sebastian?

‚ÄúWell... Yes, to a degree.‚Äù

‚ÄúSo, basically, that means you‚Äôve got information ‚Äòbout a bunch of other countries, then. Well, in that case, there‚Äôs somethin‚Äô I was hopin‚Äô ya could tell me about the Kingdom of Elfrieden.‚Äù

‚ÄúAbout the Kingdom of Elfrieden?‚Äù

The Kingdom of Elfrieden was one of the countries that neighbored the Principality of Amidonia. What was more, around fifty years ago the Principality had lost nearly half its territory in a war with the Kingdom and because of that, among other things, they were regarded as a bitter enemy.

‚ÄúI know a bit myself. He‚Äôs that hero they summoned from another world, yeah? ‚ÄúTrue enough, I haven‚Äôt heard any stories like that about the king in question.‚Äù

‚ÄúI know, right? My old man thinks some inexperienced young pup‚Äôs been put on the throne, and he‚Äôs right and ready to take advantage, but... Somethin‚Äô bugs me about it. I‚Äôve heard their last king was a mediocre leader and too nice for his own good, but would he really hand over his throne so easily if this guy was just some kid?‚Äù

‚Äú...I suppose not.‚Äù

Roroa was clever. She had a greater ability to see through to the heart of matters than either her father or brother. Roroa had accurately seen through to the core of Souma‚Äôs policy. By increasing the fluidity of distribution he meant to adjust for surpluses and shortages of supply. Roroa wiped her eyes and caught her breath.

‚ÄúYep! This new king Souma‚Äôs got my attention. Sebastian, would you mind usin‚Äô your network to get me as much info on Souma as you can?‚Äù

‚ÄúI don‚Äôt mind, but... What‚Äôs in it for me?‚Äù

‚ÄúThink of it as an investment in the future. I‚Äôm pretty sure...‚Äù

‚ÄïWe‚Äôre gonna make a killin‚Äô on this.

As she spoke those words, Roroa wore a daring smile.

Aisha: Day of Departure

It happened in the vast wooded region in the south of the Elfrieden Kingdom, also known as the God-Protected Forest.

This forest, said to be protected by a god-beast, was also the domain of the dark elves.

With great martial prowess, they took pride in their role as woodland protectors and thought of themselves as a people who lived and died with the forest. They did not socialize with other races, and, while they were a part of the kingdom, that was only because they had determined that, should the kingdom fall, the God-Protected Forest would be in danger.

However, recently, the situation in the forest had changed. Ordinarily, entry into the God-Protected Forest was forbidden to all but those of the dark elf race, but now the members of other races in the kingdom had begun to trespass. The cause of this was the food crisis that had arisen after the appearance of the Demon Lord‚Äôs Domain. Other races in the vicinity, struggling to find anything to eat, had begun to enter the forest in search of its natural bounty.

However, the forest‚Äôs bounty was not without limit. The dark elves could understand that the food crisis was making life difficult for these people, but they needed the forest‚Äôs bounty to sustain themselves. As a result, there were clashes on the outskirts of the forest between dark elves guarding against intrusion and members of other races intent on entering the forest.

If things were left to follow their own course, there was the risk that this could develop into a larger armed conflict. Something had to be done.

Having resolved to do just that, one young woman was about to depart from the forest.

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

‚ÄúGoodbye, Father. I will return soon,‚Äù said a girl with light brown skin who looked to be 18 or 19, slinging a great sword over her back.

This was Aisha Udgard, the only daughter of Wodan Udgard, chief of the dark elf village.

‚ÄúI swear that I will emerge victorious in the martial arts tournament and stand before the king,‚Äù Aisha added, thumping her chest once with pride.

Recently, it seemed the throne had passed from one king to the next. What was more, they had heard that the new king was now casting a wide net in search of talented people. As part of that process, he would be holding the Best in the Kingdom Martial Arts Tournament, where fighters would compete to demonstrate their gift of martial ability. If she won this tournament, she would be able to attend an award ceremony held by the king himself. In other words, she could meet the king in person. If she had that chance, she could make an appeal to him about the plight of the forest.

The clashes are already beginning to escalate beyond what we can handle ourselves. I must have the new king take steps to prevent intrusions!

That was Aisha‚Äôs plan.

‚Äú...Must you go?‚Äù As he watched her leave, Wodan seemed concerned. ‚ÄúA direct appeal to the king will be seen as an affront. This young man, Souma, he‚Äôs just recently taken the throne. There‚Äôs no telling what decision he will hand down. There‚Äôs no need for one so young as you to go, is there?‚Äù

Seeing her father‚Äôs concern, Aisha silently shook her head. ‚ÄúFather, you know how capable I am in battle. I am the strongest in our village. It should be possible for me to win the tournament and meet with the king. There, I will appeal to him directly about the plight of our forest.‚Äù

‚ÄúHmph! A human king will never listen to our requests,‚Äù a contemptuous voice said. This was Wodan‚Äôs younger brother (Aisha‚Äôs uncle), Robthor, who had also come to see her off. Robthor had always been a conservative, but lately, every time there had been a clash, he had taken the warriors with him and headed to the site. This had led him to develop a mistrust of other races.

‚ÄúUncle, first we must meet with him and talk,‚Äù Aisha said. ‚ÄúFortunately, I have heard the new king is a wise one.‚Äù

‚ÄúYou are too optimistic,‚Äù her uncle retorted. ‚ÄúYou may find that he is cunning instead.‚Äù

‚ÄúAll the same, I must first see for myself what kind of man he is.‚Äù

‚ÄúHmph! Do as you will.‚Äù

With those words, Robthor walked off in a huff. With a bitter smile at his younger brother‚Äôs behavior, Wodan placed a hand on Aisha‚Äôs shoulder.

‚ÄúRegardless, I just ask you come home to me safely. No matter what the result, I will not fault you for it. So long as you return safely, that is all I ask.‚Äù

‚ÄúYes! Absolutely!‚Äù Aisha nodded firmly, and Wodan nodded back.

‚ÄúThat said,‚Äù he continued, taking on a look of concern, ‚Äúyou‚Äôve never left the forest before, have you? That‚Äôs what worries me.‚Äù

‚ÄúWhat is there to fear? Even among the men of this village, none can match my strength.‚Äù

‚ÄúNot all of the dangers in the outside world come from those hostile to you.‚Äù Wodan tried to put it in terms Aisha would understand. ‚ÄúAisha, you are an excellent warrior. However, you are something of a glutton.‚Äù

‚ÄúA-Am I, really...?‚Äù

‚ÄúIf someone in the outside were to treat you to delicious food, might you not carelessly follow them wherever they took you?‚Äù

‚ÄúI-I will not forget my task!‚Äù Aisha protested, but Wodan didn‚Äôt seem too inclined to believe her.

‚ÄúThen what of when your task is complete? What if the one offering you food is a man? If a man tames you with food, will you so wish to be with him that you no longer desire to return to the forest?‚Äù

Now his complaints had just turned into those of a father worried that his daughter might hang around with bad men, so Aisha responded indignantly, ‚ÄúI will never take a man weaker than myself as my husband! And I will not be tamed with food!‚Äù

‚ÄúReally, now...‚Äù

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs true! I swear, I will not give in to the temptation of food!‚Äù

‚ÄúO-Okay...‚Äù

Somehow... this seems like a lost cause, Wodan seemed to be thinking.

‚ÄúHave a little more faith in me!‚Äù Aisha said indignantly. ‚Äú...Now, I must be going!‚Äù

And so, Aisha departed from the God-Protected Forest.

Later, Wodan received a messenger kui (something like a messenger pigeon) from Aisha. In the letter, it said that she had won the tournament, and had been able to make her appeal to the king as planned. It said that the king had given a favorable response, and that she had not been faulted for appealing to him directly. Furthermore, it said that he had offered valuable insight into how to manage the forest.

...It said all of these things, but they only accounted for about two-tenths of what she had written. Of the remaining eight-tenths, two-tenths extolled how marvelous the new king was, five-tenths related how delicious all of the foods she had eaten while staying with His Majesty, and her report on recent happenings made up less than one-tenth of the letter.

While Wodan was relieved his daughter had completed her task successfully, he knew that what he feared had come to pass, and let out a deep sigh as her father.

‚ÄúSigh... well, she seems cheerful, I suppose that is good enough,‚Äù Wodan muttered, looking towards the capital.

‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá„ÄÄ‚óá

Around that time, Aisha‚Äôs voice rang out cheerfully from the Parnam Castle cafeteria: ‚ÄúYour Majesty, seconds please!‚Äù

Juna - Better Days Are Coming

The royal capital of the Elfrieden Kingdom, Parnam.

The singing cafe Lorelei stood on one corner of the shopping street in this castle town.

This business, with its headquarters in Duchess Excel Walter‚Äôs Lagoon City, was a popular one which allowed its customers to enjoy tea and snacks by day and alcohol in a stylish atmosphere by night as they listened to the beautiful singing voices of the songstresses who worked there.

There was one songstress whose popularity was top class even by their standards; a blue-haired diva said to be descended from loreleis, Juna Doma.

Her beautiful face ensnared all who gazed upon it, her every gesture carried a quiet elegance, and her singing voice was strong and beautiful.

Liscia: Picking an Outfit

‚ÄúAugh! What should I wear?!‚Äù

In a room in the castle in Parnam, capital of the Elfrieden Kingdom, Liscia was going over the contents of her dresser while muttering to herself.

This was Liscia‚Äôs bedroom. Because of her long years in officers‚Äô school and military service, along with her own strong-willed and too-serious personality, it didn‚Äôt look anything like what you would expect from the room of a seventeen-year-old girl.

Technically, she had once been this country‚Äôs princess, and so she did have gorgeous dresses, and because she tended to take good care of her possessions, the dolls her parents had given her long ago were safely stored in her dresser, but it was very true to Liscia‚Äôs personality that she didn‚Äôt leave such things out in the open.

Yet Liscia, with her level-headed personality, was now scattering her clothes all over the room. The cause of this lay in the words from the man who was the (provisional) current king of this country, as well as Liscia‚Äôs betrothed, Souma.

‚ÄúWe‚Äôve got a day off. How about we go on a date in the castle town?‚Äù

Ever since Souma had been given the throne by her father, Albert, he had been grinding his bones to dust, working his very hardest. She knew that was why Prime Minister Hakuya had to force him to take a day off. Even from what she had seen herself, Liscia knew Souma was working too hard.

But, still... suddenly being asked on a date had left Liscia in a state of confusion and disarray.

Liscia had never had any serious romantic prospects before. In her years at the Officers‚Äô Academy, there had been many sons of the nobility who had cosied up to her because of her status, but their ulterior motives had been plain to see, and so none of them had ever measured up to the straight-laced Liscia‚Äôs expectations. Before she knew it, she had become more popular with the girls than the boys, and her status as an unattainable romantic conquest had earned her the nickname ‚ÄúThe Golden Ice Palace.‚Äù

Honestly, Liscia thought that reputation was overblown. She wasn‚Äôt pushing the boys away. There were just no worthwhile boys. As proof of that, now that she had been asked out on a date by a boy she was starting to develop feelings for, she was losing her head over it.

‚ÄúHey, Serina, Tomoe, what outfit do you think would look good on me?‚Äù

Liscia held up two outfits for the two of them to examine. Tomoe was a mystic wolf girl who had recently become her adopted sister, and Serina, her personal maid, was like a big sister to Liscia. The two of them had been watching Liscia, and Serina had found the scene half-heartwarming and half-exasperating to see.

‚ÄúUm... Everything looks good on you, Big Sister,‚Äù Tomoe ventured. ‚ÄúAnd I think... no matter which you wear, Big Brother Souma will say you look good in it.‚Äù

Tomoe had offered some harmless and inoffensive words of encouragement. Serina, on the other hand...

‚ÄúIf you are clinging to a ten-year-old girl for support, that is truly pitiful.‚Äù

...her words were blunt.

‚ÄúUrkh...‚Äù Liscia muttered. ‚ÄúFine, you choose for me, Serina.‚Äù

‚ÄúWhat are you saying? You choosing the clothes for yourself is what gives them meaning. Your feelings for the man in your heart, and how you wish to be seen by him, will make themselves evident in the clothing you select.‚Äù

‚ÄúTh-The man in my heart... Souma‚Äôs not like that, not yet...‚Äù

‚ÄúIf you dawdle too long, your position as his first queen will be snatched away by another wife he takes later,‚Äù Serina said briskly. ‚ÄúI know... perhaps I should present myself before His Majesty? Dressed up in an outfit that I selected myself?‚Äù

‚ÄúY-You can‚Äôt!‚Äù Liscia exclaimed.

‚ÄúHee hee, I was joking. Look how flustered you are. It‚Äôs simply adorable.‚Äù

‚ÄúGeez!‚Äù

Serina was a capable maid, but she had a bad habit of bullying cute girls. In other words, she was a total sadist. But rather than inflict physical pain, she preferred to toy with them psychologically and embarrass them with her words. These days, the one who received the most of her ‚Äúaffection‚Äù was Liscia.

‚ÄúH-How does this outfit look?‚Äù Liscia asked, holding up a brightly colored women‚Äôs military uniform. It was something that wouldn‚Äôt have looked out of place in a theatrical production about the French Revolution.

Serina buried her face in her palm. ‚ÄúWhy... Why is it a military uniform?‚Äù

‚ÄúB-Because Souma said... I look good in them, maybe?‚Äù

The embarrassed way Liscia said that was full of maidenly charm, and a feast for Serina‚Äôs eyes, but...

‚ÄúA military uniform simply will not do,‚Äù Serina said with a sigh. ‚ÄúIt is true that you look good in them, but that‚Äôs no outfit to be wearing on a romantic tryst. Besides which, on a special day like this, rather than let him see you the way you usually are, do you not think it would be better to show him a different side of yourself?‚Äù

‚ÄúA different... side of myself...‚Äù Liscia murmured.

‚ÄúTomoe. How does the princess look from your perspective?‚Äù

‚ÄúShe‚Äôs brave and cool,‚Äú Tomoe said, her eyes sparkling.

Serina nodded in agreement. ‚ÄúYes. That is how other people see you, princess. Now, if the cool, brave princess were to show a side of herself that was different from usual, do you not think that might seize His Majesty Souma‚Äôs heart?‚Äù

‚ÄúA side of myself that‚Äôs different from usual...‚Äù Liscia murmured.

‚ÄúFor instance, I know... Why not go with something more sensuous?‚Äù With those words, Serina pulled out a red cocktail dress. It had an open back, and had quite the risque neckline, as well.

While she owned dresses like these for social events, Liscia couldn‚Äôt imagine that they suited her, and she had never once worn it. ‚ÄúY-You want me to wear this?!‚Äù

‚ÄúNormally, you have yourself wrapped up so tightly,‚Äù Serina said. ‚ÄúThat does make it fun to get you undressed later, but why not try keeping his eyes glued to you by showing off some of that sexiness you normally wouldn‚Äôt?‚Äù

‚ÄúI‚Äôm sensing an indecent aura from every word you say! And, hold on, I‚Äôm worrying about what to wear on a date here! I couldn‚Äôt wear a thing like this around town!‚Äù

‚ÄúWell, true enough, they would mistake you for a lady of the night, I‚Äôm sure,‚Äù Serina nodded.

‚ÄúYou recommended it knowing that?!‚Äù

‚ÄúIn that case... What do you think of this one?‚Äù

Ignoring Liscia‚Äôs protestations, Serina pulled out another outfit. It was a pink one-piece dress with lots of white frills.

‚ÄúTh-That‚Äôs...‚Äù

That one-piece had been something her mother had practically forced her to accept as a present about half a year ago. Probably, she had been worried for the masculine Liscia, and ‚ÄúBecome a girl who will look good in this‚Äù had been the message she had wanted to give her out of motherly concern. However, because it wasn‚Äôt to Liscia‚Äôs taste, she had buried it in the back of the closet without so much as trying it on.

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs cutesy, I suppose you could call it,‚Äù Serina said. ‚ÄúThis could help to develop a whole new side to yourself, princess.‚Äù

‚ÄúI don‚Äôt want to let it do that! All those frills are absolutely dreadful!‚Äù

‚ÄúI think you would look adorable in it, like a doll...‚Äù

‚ÄúNo! Never!‚Äù

After that, they pulled out many outfits, arguing back and forth over them. At last, Tomoe, who was hesitantly watching from the sidelines, raised a hand to speak.

‚ÄúUm...‚Äù

‚ÄúAh, what is it, Tomoe?‚Äù Liscia asked.

‚ÄúUm... You two are both very famous. If you‚Äôre going to the castle town, don‚Äôt you need to wear clothes that won‚Äôt stand out too much?‚Äù

Liscia was silent.

Now that she mentioned it, she was right. Hakuya had been saying something about showing off how close they were to the people, but if the future king and queen were just walking around in broad daylight, it would cause a stir. In other words, she shouldn‚Äôt have been picking out a suitable outfit for a date, she should have been picking out clothes that wouldn‚Äôt make it obvious who she was. Liscia‚Äôs legs gave out, and she collapsed to a floor that was littered with clothing.

As she looked on, Serina, who had realized this the entire time, wore a beaming smile.
